 5 
1. The supervision timer expires. In such case the O-RU performs Supervision Failure handling as described in Chapter 6 
11.1.1. 7 
2. The NETCONF client terminates the subscription to the supervision-notification. The NETCONF client can either 8 
close the subscription session, terminate the NETCONF session or remove subscription to supervision notification 9 
stream. In such case the O-RU performs Supervision Termination handling as described in Chapter 11.1.2 10 
 11 
3.7 Closing a NETCONF Session 12 
A NETCONF client closes an existing NETCONF session by issuing the RPC close-session command. The O-RU shall respond 13 
and close the SSH session or TLS connection. The O-RU shall then re-commence call home procedures, as described in Section 14 
3.2. 15 
Note, under normal operations, it is expected that at least one NETCONF session with “sudo” or “hybrid-odu” privileges are 16 
long-lived and used to repeatedly reset the O-RU’s supervision watchdog timer. NECTONF clients associated with other  17 
privilege groups are not expected to operate using persistent NETCONF sessions. 18 
Note, if a NETCONF client has been previously become known to an O -RU by being configured using NETCONF, and the 19 
NETCONF client is  subsequently removed from the O -RU’s configuration, e.g., by a second NETCONF client with “sudo” 20 
privileges, the NETCONF server shall force the termination of the NETCONF session to the removed client.  21 
3.8 PNF Registration  22 
The support by an O-RU of PNF Registration to a discovered Event-Collector is optional and hence this section only applies to 23 
those O-RUs that support this optional capability. An O-RU that support pnfRegistration shall also support the Monitoring the 24 
Communications Channel between O-RU and Event-Collector as defined in sub-section 15.6. 25 
3.8.1 PNF Registration Procedure 26 
The pnfRegistration notification is a JSON encoded message sent from the O -RU to the discovered Event-Collector using 27 
REST/HTTPS. As a pre -condition to performing PNF Re gistration, the O -RU first receives the Event -Collector information 28 
encoded in a DHCP/DHCPv6 option as described in sub-section 3.1.6. The O-RU shall attempt to establish a HTTP connection 29 
to the discovered Event-Collector using TLS to authenticate the connection. It shall then signal the pnfRegistration notification 30 
over the HTTP/TLS connection . The sending of the pnfRegistration notification is repeated periodically until the SMO 31 
establishes a NETCONF session with the O-RU. 32 
An O -RU that is performing the PNF registration procedure whilst simultaneously performing the call home procedure 33 
described in sub-section 3.2, shall be able to determine that the SMO has established a NETCONF session with the O-RU. This 34 
is identified by the O-RU analyzing the source IP address from which the NETCONF originates, based on the assumption that 35 
the NETCONF session from the SMO originates from an IP address that is distinct from the IP address(es ) of the “known O-36 
RU Controller(s)” to which the O-RU is simultaneously performing the call home procedure.  37

to the version of pnfRegistration fields. 11

Chapter 4 O-RU to O-DU Interface Management  2 
An O -RU has a number of network interfaces, including Ethernet , VLAN  and IP interfaces . This section describes the 3 
management of these network interfaces.  4 
4.1 O-RU Interfaces 5 
The O-RU’s configuration for its interfaces is defined using the o-ran-interfaces.yang module. This module augments the 6 
standard ietf -interfaces.yang and ietf -ip.yang modules. The O-RU’s interfaces are built on a layering principle  where each 7 
interface has a unique name.  8 
All interfaces are referenced by their port-number and name. The base interface corresponds to the Ethernet interface. These 9 
leafs describe the maximum transmission unit (l2-mtu), the hardware-address as well as optional alias mac addressees that may 10 
be used to transport the CU plane. Above the Ethernet interface are VLAN interfaces. Both Ethernet and VLAN interfaces can 11 
support IP interfaces. IP interfaces are defined using the standard ietf -ip.yang model. Accordingly, each IP interface can have 12 
an IPv4 and/or IPv6 interface(s) defined. Operational state associated with these interfaces provide additional detail of the layer 13 
3 configuration, including prefix(es), domain name servers and default gateway addresses. 14 
Finally, leafs associated with CoS and DSCP marking are defined, enabling independent configuration of CoS and DSCP 15 
markings for u-plane, c -plane and m -plane traffic. As a default, all user -plane flows are marked identically by the O-RU. 16 
Optionally, the interfaces can be configured to support enhanced user plane marking for up -link traffic whereby different CoS 17 
or DSCP values can be configured. This enables individual receive endpoints in the O-RU to be configured with different 18 
markings to then enable differentiated handling of up-link flows by the transport system. 19 
Because the o-ran-interfaces model defines augments to the ietf -interfaces model, the O-RU can leverage the definition of 20 
operational state in ietf-interfaces to optionally report packet and byte counts on a per interface basis. A single RPC is defined 21 
in the o-ran-interfaces module, to enable these counters to be reset. 22 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          46 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
4.2 Transceiver 1 
The o-ran-transceiver YANG module is used to define operational state for the pluggable transceiver module (like SFP, SFP+, 2 
SFP28, XFP and QSFP, QSFP+, QSFP28, QSFP56 ). Each transceiver is associated with a unique interface-name and port-3 
number. 4 
A digital diagnostic monitoring interface for optical transceivers is used to allow access to device operating parameters. As 5 
specified in SFF-8472 [16] and SFF-8636 [34], data is typically retrieved from the transceiver module in a file. This file may 6 
be obtained from O-RU by the NETCONF client. Please see Chapter 9 for more details. 7 
With QSFP form factor, the opt ical links may be multi -wavelengths (4xTx & 4xRx) and/or multi -fibers (MPO - Multifiber 8 
Parallel Optic). The QSFP digital diagnostic interface [34] describes the use of optical lanes and the O -RU interface 9 
management defines alarm 29 :“transceiver fault” for all media lanes. 10 
The byte with offset i (i=0, …, 511) from the beginning of the file is the byte read from data address i of the transceiver memory 11 
at two-wire interface address 0xA0 if i<256, otherwise it is the byte read from data address i-256 of the transceiver memory at 12 
two-wire interface address 0xA2. The retrieved data is stored in the file without any conversion in binary format. 13 
The O-RU stores data from the transceiver module on transceiver module detection during startup. The data from the transceiver 14 
module is saved in the file. A NETCONF client can upload it by using the File Upload procedure defined in chapter 9. The O-15 
RU does not synchronize contents of the file with transceiver memory in runtime, therefore bytes representing dynamic 16 
information are expected to be outdated . The O-RU does not remove the file on transceiver module removal. If a transceiver 17 
module is inserted during File Upload procedure then the procedure may provide a file with previous content or fail (with failure 18 
reason as listed in File Upload procedure). If the O-RU is unable to retrieve the data from the transceiver module or it is not 19 
present then the O-RU does not create the file or removes the file created earl ier (note that File Upload procedure requesting 20 
non-existing file shall fail).  21 
The file name shall have the following syntax: 22 
sfp_{portNumber}.sffcap 23 
where {portNumber} is the value of port-number leaf of the corresponding list of port -transceiver data. E xamples: 24 
sfp_0.sffcap, sfp_1.sffcap. 25 
4.3 C/U Plane VLAN Configuration 26 
Within the o-ran-interfaces YANG model, each named Ethernet interface includes a leaf to indicate whether VLAN tagging is 27 
supported. By default, VLAN tagging is enabled on all interfaces . This permits an O-RU to autonomously discover that it is 28 
connected to a trunk port, as described in Section 3.1.2. 29 
When an O-RU is connected to a trunk port, VLANs will also typically be assigned to the C/U plane connections. The VLAN(s) 30 
used to support C/U plane transport may be different from the VLAN(s) used to support management plane connectivity. The 31 
VLAN assigned to the U-Plane must be the same as the VLAN assigned to the C-Plane for any given eAxC_ID. When different 32 
VLANs are used, the C/U plane V LANs shall be configured in the O-RU by the NETCONF client. In such circumstances, as 33 
defined in o-ran-interfaces, the NETCONF client shall configure separate named interfaces for each active VLAN. This 34 
configuration will define a C/U-Plane named VLAN interface as being the higher-layer-if reference for the underlying Ethernet 35 
interface and the underlying Ethernet interface is defined as being the lower-layer-if reference for the named VLAN interface. 36 
4.4 O-RU C/U Plane IP Address Assignment 37 
In this release, the support for C/U plane transport over UDP/IP is optional and hence this section only applies to those O-RUs 38 
that support this optional capability. 39 
An O-RU that supports C/U plane transport over UDP/IP shall support IPv4 and /or IPv6 based transport. A NETCONF client 40 
can receive a hint as to whether an O-RU supports a particular IP version by using the get rpc to recover the list of interfaces 41 
supported by the O-RU and using the presence of the augmented ipv4 container or ipv6 container in the o-ran-interfaces YANG 42 
module as an indication that a particular IP version is supported. 43 
The IP interface(s) used to support UDP/IP based C/U plane transport may be different than the IP interface(s) used to support 44 
management plane connectivity. When different IP interface(s) is/are used, the C/U plane IP interfaces shall be configured in  45 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          47 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
the O-RU by the NETCONF client by using the ietf-ip YANG model to configure the IPv4 container and/or IPv6 container. 1 
When defined by the NETCONF client, this interface shall be configured using either a named Ethernet interface (i.e., where 2 
the interface type is set to ianaift:ethernetCsmacd) and/or a named VLAN interface  (i.e., where the interface type is set to 3 
ianaift:l2vlan), depending upon whether VLANs are used to support IP based C/U plane traffic. 4 
When a separate C/U plane IP interface is configured by the NETCONF client, additionally the NETCONF client may statically 5 
configure the IP address(es) on this/these interface(s). If the NETCONF client does not statically configure an IP address, the 6 
O-RU shall be responsible for performing IP address assignment procedures on the configured interfaces. 7 
When an O-RU has not been configured with a static IP address , the O-RU shall support the IP address assignment using the 8 
following techniques: 9 
When the O-RU supports IPv4: 10 
1. IPv4 configuration using DHCPv4 [10]. 11 
and when the O-RU supports IPv6: 12 
2. IPv6 Stateless Address Auto-Configuration (SLAAC) [11]. 13 
3. IPv6 State-full address configuration uses DHCPv6 [12]. 14 
4.5 Definition of processing elements 15 
The CU-plane application needs to be uniquely associated with specific data flows. This association is achieved by defining an 16 
O-RU “processing element” which can then be associated with a particular C /U plane endpoint address [2] or delay 17 
measurement operation. Unless specified otherwise, a common processing element is required to be configured for the control 18 
and user-plane application components associated with any individual eAxC_ID. 19 
The O-RU management plane supports different options for defining the transport -based endpoint identifiers used by a 20 
particular processing element (used depending on transport environment), supporting the following 3 options: 21 
• Processing element definition based on usage of different (alias) MAC addresses; 22 
• Processing element definition based on a combination of VLAN identity and MAC address; and 23 
• Processing element definition based on UDP-ports and IP addresses. 24 
Note: there is no well-defined source port currently allocated by IANA for the o-ran application and hence the NETCONF 25 
client is responsible for configuring this port number in the O-RU.  26 
A processing element defines both the local and remote endpoints used with a specific data flow. The processing eleme nt 27 
definition includes its element name which is then used by other systems to refer to a particular processing element instance. 28 
The o-ran-interfaces YANG model is used to define feature support for C/U plane transport based on alias MAC addresses and 29 
UDP/IP. The exchange of NETCONF capabilities is used to signal which optional capabilities are supported by the O-RU, as 30 
described in Annex C. 31 
The o-ran-processing-elements YANG model uses a processing-elements container to define a list of processing elements. 32 
Each processing element is identified by a unique element  name. Each processing element references a particular interface-33 
name used to support the data flows associated with a particular processing elemen t. Depending upon the type of C/U plane 34 
transport session, additionally leafs are configured that specify MAC addresses, and/or VLANs and/or IP addresses and/or UDP 35 
ports used to identify a particular processing element. 36 
The O-RU may discard any received CU-plane messages , i.e., eCPRI/IEEE 1914 frames/packets, which are not transported 37 
using a configured processing element. 38 
4.6 O-DU Verification of C/U Plane Transport Connectivity  39 
As described above, there will likely be multiple C/U -plane data flows being exchanged between the O-DU and the O-RU. In 40 
order to enable checks verifying end -to-end transport connectivity between the O-DU and O-RU, the O-RU shall support 41 
transport connectivity check capabilities using a request/reply function.  42 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          48 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Using that connectivity monitoring procedure, reachability/connectivity checks between user plane endpoints can be performed 1 
by the O-DU: 2 
- During O-RU configuration, to validate the transport configuration 3 
- At runtime to monitor network connectivity 4 
In packet networks connectivity checking is usually done by exchanging probe-messages between the endpoints. The periodicity 5 
of this exchange depends on the use case. For availability measurement, the only use case relevant for this specification, the 6 
periodicity is usually between 1 and 60 seconds. 7 
Two different network protocols are defined for performing the transport connectivity check procedure: 8 
- For C/U sessions over Ethernet: Loop -back Protocol (LB/LBM) as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802 .1ag) 9 
[17]. 10 
- When the O-RU supports C/U sessions over IP: UDP echo, RFC 862 [18]. 11 
 12 
Figure 9: C/U Plane Transport Connectivity Verification 13 
4.6.1 Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 14 
If the O-RU and O-DU are operating their C/U sessions on Ethernet, the transport connectivity verification checks operate at 15 
the Ethernet layer. In this O-RU Management Plane Specification, the protocol for Ethernet connectivity monitoring is based 16 
on the Loop-back Protocol as defined by IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag) [17].  17 
For the purpose of connectivity monitoring all C/U -plane messaging endpoints in the fronthaul network are part of the same 18 
Maintenance Entity (ME). They each get the assigned the role of a Maintenance association End Point (MEP) for LBM. 19 
The sending of Loop-back Messages (LBMs) is administratively initiated and stopped in the O-DU. Therefore, sending LBM 20 
requests needs to be requested by an administration entity, specifying an Ethernet MAC address assigned to the O-RU responder. 21 
In this O-RU Management Plane Specification requests are always sent from an O-DU to a unicast Ethernet MAC address of 22 
an O-RU. 23 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          49 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
4.6.1.1 Validating the transport configuration 1 
After setting up a U/C-plane session between an O-DU and an O-RU, the O-DU can test whether connectivity exists as per the 2 
configuration. To achieve that, at the time a U/C-plane messaging endpoint becomes operational at an O-RU, it starts an LBM 3 
responder application which automatically responds to incoming LBM requests on that endpoint. Based on a configuration 4 
command the O-DU starts sending out a predefined number of LBM requests to its O-RU(s) at a predefined interval, storing 5 
the information received in LBM responses from the O-RU(s) in an internal database. O-RU(s) are identified by both Ethernet 6 
MAC address and the CU plane VLAN.  7 
Note, the O-RU shall be able to respond to Loop back Messages received from different remote Maintenance Association 8 
Endpoints 9 
In case the configuration of the session is indeed correct, the O-DU should receive LBM responses from the O-RU(s) within a 10 
time frame dependent on the network latency and the O-RU’s reaction time. If LBMs from the O-RU(s) are being received, the 11 
session is determined to be operational. 12 
4.6.1.2 Monitor network connectivity 13 
After the procedure described in section 4.6.1.1 has been executed successfully, a further procedure may be executed 14 
continuously to maintain the connectivity status. To achieve this the O-DU continues to send out LBM requests at the configured 15 
interval. It also keeps track of LBM responses received.  16 
Based on the LBM responses received the O-DU shall decide on the connectivity status. Connectivity shall be assumed to be 17 
available as long as L BM responses from the O-RU(s) are being received at the configured interval. Connectivity shall be 18 
assumed not available if no LBM response from the particular O-RU has been received for an interval that is as long as 3 x the 19 
configured LBM request interval or longer. 20 
4.6.1.3 Managing Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure 21 
An O-DU may have one or more Ethernet interfaces that have to support the Ethernet connectivity monitoring procedure. This 22 
section describes the management of this function. The module described here is based on (i.e. a subset of) the mef-cfm module 23 
defined by the Metro Ethernet Forum [19]. This is to allow for a later extension of the module to the full feature set of mef-cfm.  24 
The YANG module provided below supports the configuration and fault management of the Loop-back Protocol as defined by 25 
IEEE 802.1Q (amendment 802.1ag). 26 
Derived from MEF CFM YANG, the subset of type definitions is defined as part of the o-ran-lbm.yang. 27 
4.6.2 IP connectivity monitoring procedure 28 
If the O-RU and O-DU are connected using IP (and UDP/IP is being used to transport the C/U plane), these transport 29 
connectivity verification checks operate at layer 3. Layer 3 connection verification is based on the O-RU supporting the UDP 30 
echo server functionality, RFC 862 [18]. The NETCONF client is responsible for enabling the UDP echo server in the O-RU, 31 
triggering the O-RU to listen for UDP datagrams on the well-known port 7. When a datagram is received by the O-RU, the data 32 
from it is sent back towards the sender, where its receipt can be used to confirm UDP/IP connectivity between the endpoints. 33 
4.6.2.1 Managing IP Connectivity Monitoring Procedure 34 
This section describes the management of the UDP echo functionality. The NETCONF client uses the enable-udp-echo leaf in 35 
the udp-echo YANG model to control operation of the UDP echo server in the O-RU. The NETCONF client is able to control 36 
the DSCP marking used by the O-RU when it echoes back datagrams using the dscp-config leaf. Additionally, the NETCONF 37 
client can recover the number of UDP Echo messages sent by the O-RU by using echo-replies-transmitted operational state. 38 
An O-DU may have one or more IP interfaces that have to support the UDP/IP connectivity monitoring procedure . An O-RU 39 
with its UDP echo server enabled shall be able to respond to UDP datagrams originated from any valid source IP address. 40 
4.7 C/U-Plane Delay Management  41 
The Intra-PHY lower layer fronthaul split has the characteristic of a stringent bandwidth and tight latency requirement. The 42 
CUS-Plane specification [2] describes how the propagation delay incurred due to distance between the O-DU and O-RU is an 43 
important parameter in defining the optimization of windowing and receive -side buffering operations. Thi s section describes 44 
the procedures that are used to manage the delay parameters for the fronthaul split.  45 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          50 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
4.7.1 Delay Parameters 1 
The reference points for delay management are introduced in the CUS-Plane Specification [2], specifically the sub -sections 2 
entitled “Latency Requirements” and “O -RU External Delay Handling”.  Important delay parameters related to the operation 3 
of the O-RU are referred to as the O-RU delay profile. As the delay characteristics for an O-RU may vary based on air interface 4 
properties, a table of the parameters is provided based on a combination of sub -carrier spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth. 5 
Other parameters related to delays to external antennas may vary according to specific tx/rx-array-carriers. When considering 6 
the downlink data direction, these parameters include: 7 
T2a_min :  Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving the last data sample over the 8 
fronthaul interface and transmitting the first IQ sample at the antenna. 9 
T2a_max: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a data packet is received before the corresponding fi rs IQ 10 
sample is transmitted at the antenna. 11 
Using the above parameters, (T2a_max – T2a_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 12 
reception window range. 13 
T2a_min_cp_dl: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving downlink real time control 14 
plane message over the fronthaul interface and transmitting the corresponding first IQ sample at the antenna. 15 
T2a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest allowable time when a downlink real time control message is received before 16 
the corresponding first IQ sample is transmitted at the antenna. 17 
Tcp_adv_dl: Corresponding to the time difference (advance) between the reception window for downlink real time Control 18 
messages and reception window for the corresponding IQ data messages. 19 
Tda: Corresponding to the time difference between the output of DL signal at the antenna connector of O -RU and the 20 
transmission over the air. 21 
The delay parameters related to the operation of the O-RU for the uplink data direction include: 22 
Ta3_min: Corresponding to the minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 23 
transmitting the first data sample over the fronthaul interface. 24 
Ta3_max: Corresponding to the maximum O-RU data processing delay between receiving an IQ sample at the antenna and 25 
transmitting the last data sample over the fronthaul interface. 26 
Using the above parameters, (Ta3_max – Ta3_min): The difference between these two parameters corresponds to the O-RU 27 
transmission window range. 28 
T2a_min_cp_ul: The minimum O-RU data processing delay between receiving real time up-link control plane message over 29 
the fronthaul interface and receiving the first IQ sample at the antenna. 30 
T2a_max_cp_ul: The earliest allowable time when a real time up-link control message is received before the corresponding 31 
first IQ sample is received at the antenna. 32 
Tau: Corresponding to the t ime difference between the reception over the air and the input of UL signal at the antenna 33 
connector of O-RU. 34 
When requested, all O-RUs shall signal the table of statically “pre -defined” values of the above parameters, for different 35 
supported combinations of SCS and channel bandwidth over the management plane interface. This will typically occur during 36 
the initial startup phase. 37 
4.7.2 Reception Window Monitoring 38 
The O-RU shall monitor operation of its reception window, monitoring the arrival of packets received over the fronthaul 39 
interface relative to the earliest and latest allowable times as defined by the values of T2a_max and T2a_min respectively. 40 
See Annex B.2 for information on reception window counters. 41 
4.7.3 External Antenna Delay Control 42 
An O-RU may optionally support the external antenna delay control by indicating that it supports the EXT-ANT-DELAY-43 
CONTROL feature in its o-ran-wg4-features YANG model. Such an O-RU uses the ext-ant-delay-capability schema node in 44 
o-ran-module-cap YANG model to indicate to the O -RU Controller the type of external delay configuration supported by the 45 
O-RU: 46 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          51 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
• PER-O-RU: The O-RU only supports a single value of t-da-offset and a single value of t-au-offset across all tx-array-1 
carriers and rx-array-carriers respectively. 2 
• PER-ARRAY: The O -RU supports separate values of  t-da-offset and t-au-offset across individual tx-arrays and rx -3 
arrays respectively. 4 
• PER-ARRAY-CARRIER: The O-RU supports separate values of t-da-offset and t-au-offset across separate tx-array-5 
carriers and rx-array-carriers respectively. 6 
 7 
4.8 O-RU Adaptive Delay Capability 8 
O-RUs may optionally support the ability to optimize their buffers based on information signalled concerning the configuration 9 
of the O-DU, e.g., including the O-DU delay profile, together with transport delay information, which may have been derived 10 
by the O-DU by using a delay measurement procedures operated by the O-DU or by other techniques.  This section describes 11 
such optional O-RU buffer optimization functionality.  12 
An O-RU that supports the optional adaptive timing capability shall indicate such to the O-RU Controller client by exchanging 13 
NETCONF capabilities, as described in Section 6.2 and Annex C indicating that it supports the ADAPTIVE-O-RU-PROFILE 14 
feature. An O-RU Controller may then provide the O-RU with the O-DU delay profile based on a combination of sub -carrier 15 
spacing (SCS) and channel bandwidth, comprising the following parameters: 16 
T1a_max_up: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O-DU can support transmitting an IQ data message 17 
prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna 18 
TXmax: Corresponding to the maximum amount of time which the O-DU requires to transmit all downlink user plane IQ 19 
data message for a symbol. 20 
Ta4_max: Corresponding to the latest possible time which the O-DU can support receiving the last uplink user plane IQ 21 
data message for a symbol 22 
RXmax: Corresponding to the maximum time difference the O-DU can support between receiving the first user plane I Q 23 
data message for a symbol and receiving the last user plane IQ data message for the same symbol. 24 
T1a_max_cp_dl: Corresponding to the earliest possible time which the O -DU can support transmitting the downlink real 25 
time control message prior to transmission of the corresponding IQ samples at the antenna. 26 
In addition to the O-DU delay profile, the O-RU-Controller provides the O-RU with the transport network timing parameters: 27 
T12_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-DU and O-RU processing elements 28 
T12_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-DU and O-RU processing elements 29 
T34_min: Corresponding to the minimum delay between any O-RU and O-DU processing elements 30 
T34_max:  Corresponding to the maximum delay between O-RU and O-DU processing elements 31 
Note, as per [2], the O -RU Controller shall configure values of t12-max and t34-max as if there is no external delay, i.e. 32 
Tau = Tda = 0 (zero). 33 
The O-RU may use this information to adapt its delay profile, ensuring that the inequalities defined in Annex B of [2] are still 34 
valid  35 
The O-RU controller will typically provide this information during the O-RU’s start-up procedure. If an O-RU receives the 36 
adaptive delay configuration information when operating a carrier, the O-RU shall not adapt its O-RU delay profile until all 37 
carriers operating using the O-RU buffers have been disabled. Once an O-RU has adapted its O-RU profile, it will include the 38 
newly adapted timing values when signaling its delay parameters to a NETCONF client. 39 
4.9 Measuring transport delay parameters 40 
An O-RU may optionally indicate that it supports the eCPRI based measurement of transport delays between O-DU and O-RU. 41 
If O-RU supports measured transport delay, it shall implement the protocol as described in the CUS-Plane Specification [2].  42 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          52 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
An O-RU that supports the eCPRI based delay measurement capability, shall be able to support the operation of delay 1 
measurements whenever any processing element has been configured as described in section 4.5. For each processing element 2 
configured, the O-RU shall be able to respond to any messages when received and keep a record of the number of responses, 3 
requests and follow-up messages transmitted by the O-RU. 4 
4.10 O-RU Monitoring of C/U Plane Connectivity  5 
The O-RU is responsible for monitoring the C/U plane connection and raising an alarm if the logical C/U -plane connection 6 
associated with a processing -element fails. The O -RU uses a timer to monitor the C/U plane connection on a per processing -7 
element basis. This timer is enabled only when at least one array-carrier using the processing-element is in the active state and 8 
is reset whenever it receives any C/U plane data flows associated with the particular processing-element. Because of the variety 9 
of PHY and C/U plane configurations, the O -RU cannot independently determine the minimum frequency of messages across 10 
the fronthaul interface. Therefore, as a default, the O -RU shall use a timer value of 160 milliseconds for monitoring the C/U 11 
plane connection. An O-RU may indicate that its C/U-plane monitoring timer is configurable, by the presence of the cu-plane-12 
monitoring container in the o-ran-supervision.yang model. A NETCONF client can use the container to configure the O-RU’s 13 
timer value, including being able to disable the operation of C/U Plane monitoring. 14 
Note, if the O-RU supports this timer, then depending on how long the O-DU takes to initiate sending of C/U plane data 15 
flows, it may be advisable for the NETCONF client to initially disable the operation of the timer before carrier activation. 16 
Such an approach will avoid the O-RU sending spurious alarm notifications triggered by O-DU delays in initializing the 17 
sending of C/U plane data that exceed the default timer value. Once C/U plane data flows have commenced, the NECTONF 18 
client can re-configure the timer with the desired value and hence activate monitoring of the C/U plane connectivity by the O-19 
RU. 20 
4.11 Bandwidth Management 21 
An O-RU can indicate the maximum bitrate able to be supported on those interfaces associated with a particular physical port 22 
using the optional nominal-bitrate leaf in the o -ran-transceiver YANG module. When the sustainable bitrate able to be 23 
supported by an O -RU is less than the combined bitrates of all its physical ports, an O -RU can use the optional interface-24 
grouping container in the o -ran-interfaces YANG model to define the maximum sustainable rate able to be supported by an 25 
interface-group-id corresponding to a group of one or more physical interfaces. The same YANG model is used to augment 26 
the ietf-interfaces defined interface list with the interface-group-id to which the interface belongs. 27 
Note, the maximum sustainable bandwidth is calculated over one radio frame, meaning that the peak bandwidth can 28 
exceed the defined value over time periods shorter than one radio frame. 29 
Chapter 5 Software Management 30 
The Software Management function provides a set of operations allowing the desired software build to be downloaded, installed 31 
and activated at O-RU. Successful software activation operation does not mean an O-RU is running the just activated software 32 
build. An O-RU reset RPC is required to trigger the O-RU to take the activated software build into operational use. 33 
Note: the software management function s involve the O-RU controller subscribing to receive particular YANG 34 
notifications from the O -RU. All O -RUs support the NETCONF Create-Subscription method, enabling those 35 
notifications to be transported using NETCONF notifications. In addition, those O-RUs that support the optional NON-36 
PERSISTENT-MPLANE feature, the O -RU Controller can create a configured subscription from the O -RU, enabling 37 
those notifications to be transported over HTTPS to an Event-Collector as described in Chapter 15. 38 
A single software build is considered as set of internally consistent files compliant within such a build. Replacement of files 39 
within a build is prohibited, as this will cause software version incompatibility. Software build is a subject of versioning and 40 
maintenance and as such cannot be broken. 41 
The use of compression and ciphering for the content of the software build is left to vendor implementation. The only file which 42 
shall never be ciphered is the manifest.xml file.  43 
It is also Vendor's responsibility to handle SW Build / package / file integrity check. 44 
The O-RU provides a set of so called "software slots" or "slots". Each slot provides an independent storage location for a single 45 
software build. The number of slots offered by O-RU depends on the device’s capabilities. At least two writable slots shall be 46 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          53 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
available at the O-RU for failsafe update operation. Presence of read only slot is optiona l. The software slots are resources 1 
provided by the O-RU and as such are not the subject of creation and deletion. The size of individual software slots is fixed and 2 
determined by the O-RU's vendor and sufficient to accommodate the full software build. 3 
Note: procedures used in Software Management are covered by o-ran-software-management.yang module. 4 
5.1 Software Package 5 
The software package is delivered by the O-RU vendor. 6 
Each software package includes: 7 
- manifest.xml 8 
- software files to be installed on O-RU 9 
The name of package should follow the following format: 10 
“<Vendor Code><Vendor Specific Field>[#NUMBER].EXT” 11 
Where: 12 
- Vendor Code is a mandatory part which has two capital characters, 13 
- Vendor Specific Field is any set of characters allowed in filename. The value must not include character “_” (underscore) 14 
or “#” (hash). The value can be defined per vendor for the human readable information. Version information is necessary 15 
in the Vendor Specific Field which defines load version, 16 
- NUMBER is optional and used when the original file is split into smaller pieces – number after “#” indicates the number 17 
of a piece. Numbering starts from 1 and must be continuous, 18 
- EXT is a mandatory part which defines the extension of filename. A vendor provides one or more software packages. Each 19 
software package shall be compressed by zip. 20 
Note: the name of package needs a <Vendor Code> prefix to avoid issue if two vendors provide files with same name. 21 
Note: the NETCONF client shall support ZIP functionality to enable support of compressed files types.  22 
Note: the operator needs to manage and control which O-RU files will be stored and used in the file server, e.g., based on O-23 
RU files provided by O-RU vendors and network configurations. The operator needs to make sure that only the expected version 24 
of O-RU files will be transferred from the file server to the O-RU. Different versions of files for O-RU with the same vendor 25 
and same product code should be avoided. 26 
The content of the manifest.xml file allows to maintain software update process correctly in terms of compatibility between O-27 
RU hardware and software build to be downloaded. The content of the Manifest file prohibits the O-RU from installing software 28 
builds designed for device based on different hardware. The format of the manifest.xml file is: 29 
<xml> 30 
<manifest version=”1.0”> /// @version describes version of file format (not the content) 31 
 <products> 32 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x11” name=”RUXX.x11” build-Id=”1”/>  33 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818820\.x12” name=”RUXX.x12” build-Id=”1”/> 34 
  <product vendor=”XX” code=”0818818\…” name=”RUYY” build-Id=”2”/>  35 
  /// @vendor is as reported by O-RU 36 
  /// @code is a regular expression that is checked against productCode reported by O-RU 37 
  /// @name is optional and used for human reading – MUST NOT be used for other purposes! 38 
  /// @buildId is value of build@id (see below) 39 
 </products> 40 
 <builds> 41 
  <build id=”1” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 42 
  /// @id is index of available builds. 43 
  /// @bldName and @bldVersion are used in YANG (build-name, build-version) 44 
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 45 
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 46 
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 47 
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 48 
   /// @fileName and @fileVersion are used in YANG (name, version) 49 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          54 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
   /// @path is full path (with name and extension) of a physical file, relative to package 1 
root folder,used in YANG (local-path) 2 
   /// @checksum is used to chech file integrity on O-RU side 3 
  </build> 4 
  <build id=”2” bldName=”xyz” bldVersion=”1.0”> 5 
   <file fileName=”xxxx” fileVersion=”1.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 6 
package -root-folder” checksum=”FAA898”/> 7 
   <file fileName=”yyyy” fileVersion=”2.0” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 8 
package -root-folder” checksum=”AEE00C”/ > 9 
   <file fileName=”zzzz” fileVersion=”1.5” path=”full-file_name-with-path-relative-to- 10 
package -root-folder” checksum=”ABCDEF”/ > 11 
  </build> 12 
 </builds> 13 
</manifest> 14 
</xml> 15 
 16 
Note: Keywords in manifest.xml example are in bold, the keywords must be strictly followed considering of cross-vendor cases. 17 
Note 2: Correspondence between content of manifest.xml tags and content of o-ran-software-management.yang is: 18 
- XML tag "product vendor" corresponds to content leaf "vendor-code", 19 
- XML tag "code" corresponds to content of leaf "product-code", 20 
- XML tag "build-Id" corresponds to content of leaf "build-id", 21 
- XML tag "bldName" corresponds to content of leaf "build-name", 22 
- XML tag "bldVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "build-version", 23 
- XML tag "fileName" corresponds to content of leaf "name" in list "files", 24 
-XML tag "fileVersion" corresponds to content of leaf "version" in list "files" 25 
5.2 Software Inventory 26 
Pre-condition:  27 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 28 
Post-condition: 29 
- NETCONF client successfully collected the software inventory information from NETCONF server. 30 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          55 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Figure 10: Inventory fetch call flow 2 
Software Inventory is fetched by a NETCONF Client using the NETCONF get rpc filtered over the software-slot container. 3 
The response contains information about each software slot and its contents. 4 
The following information is provided by software-inventory reply message: 5 
a) name - name of the software slot (the name is defined by the O-RU vendor) 6 
b) status - status of the software package. Status of the package can be  7 
 - VALID - Slot contains a software build considered as proven valid. 8 
 - INVALID - software build is not currently used by O-RU. The software is considered by the O-RU as damaged 9 
(e.g. wrong CRC). 10 
Activation of a software slot containing  an invalid software build shall be prohibited. Note: failed software install 11 
operation can cause a slot status to change to "Invalid". 12 
 - EMPTY - software slot does not contain a software package. Activation of an empty software slot shal l be 13 
prohibited.  14 
c) active - indicates if the software stored in particular slot is activated at the moment. 15 
 - True - software slot contains an activated software build. Active::True can be assigned only for slots with status 16 
"Valid". At any time, only one slot in the O-RU MUST be marked as Active::True. The O-RU shall reject activation 17 
for software slots with status "Empty" and "Invalid". 18 
 - False - software slot contains passive software build or is empty 19 
d) running - informs if software stored in particular slot is used at the moment. 20 
 - True - software slot contains the software build used by the O-RU in its current run. 21 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          56 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 - False - software slot contains a software build not used by O-RU at the moment. 1 
e) access – informs about access rights for the current slot 2 
- READ_ONLY – The slot is intended only for factory software. Activation of such software slot means performing 3 
a factory reset operation and a return to factory defaults settings. 4 
- READ_WRITE – slot used for updating software 5 
f) product-code - product code provided by the vendor, specific to the product. 6 
g) vendor-code - unique code of the vendor. 7 
h) build-id - Identity associated with the software build.  This id is used to find the appropriate build -version for the 8 
product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 9 
i) build-name - Name of the software build. 10 
j) build-version - Version of the software build for the product consist of the vendor-code and the product-code. 11 
k) files – list of files in build 12 
l) name – name of one particular file 13 
m) version – version of the file 14 
n) local-path - complete path of the file on local file system 15 
o) integrity - result of the file integrity check 16 
- OK – file integrity is correct 17 
- NOK – file is corrupted 18 
If a slot contains a file with integrity::NOK, the O-RU shall mark the whole slot with status::INVALID. The content of a 19 
software-slot is fully under O-RU's management - including removal of the content occupying the slot (in case the slot is subject 20 
of software update procedure), control of file system consistency and so on. The slot content shall not be removed until there is 21 
a need for new software to be installed.  22 
Note: The empty slot parameters shall be as follows 23 
name: up to vendor, not empty 24 
status: "INVALID" 25 
active: False 26 
running: False 27 
access: READ_WRITE 28 
product-code: up to vendor 29 
vendor code: up to vendor 30 
build-name: null (empty string) 31 
build-version: null (empty string) 32 
files: empty 33 
5.3 Download 34 
Pre-condition:  35 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 36 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          57 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive download-event notifications. 1 
Post-condition: 2 
- O-RU downloads all files specified and successfully stores the downloaded files in the O-RU’s file system.  3 
 4 
Figure 11: Software download call flow 5 
Following types of authentications shall be supported for software-download: 6 
a) password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 7 
Following types of authentications may be supported for software-download: 8 
 9 
b) X.509 certificate for authentication of FTPES client (O-RU) and FTPES server  10 
c) certificate for both O-RU and sFTP server authentication 11 
The software-download rpc is used to trigger the downloading of software to the O-RU. The download shall be performed 12 
using either sFTP or FTPES. The rpc specifies the URI of the remote location of the software files using the remote-file-path 13 
leaf, where the URI scheme is used to signal whether to use sFTP or FTPES. 14 
Note, an O-RU Controller shall only trigger software-download using FTPES if it is using NETCONF/TLS to 15 
configure the O-RU. 16 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          58 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
  1 
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 2 
a) STARTED – software download operation has been started 3 
b) FAILED – software download operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message  4 
When the O-RU completes the  software download or software download fail s, the O-RU shall send the download-event 5 
notification with one of the following statuses: 6 
a) COMPLETED 7 
b) AUTHENTICATION_ERROR - source available, wrong credentials 8 
c) PROTOCOL_ERROR – sFTP or FTPES protocol error 9 
d) FILE_NOT_FOUND - source not available 10 
e) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason  11 
f) TIMEOUT - source available, credentials OK, Operation timed out  (e.g. source becomes unavailable durin g ongoing 12 
operation). 13 
The above will be repeated until all files which are required for the O-RU and which belong to the software package have been 14 
downloaded to the O-RU. 15 
5.4 Install 16 
Pre-condition:  17 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 18 
- At least one software slot with status active::False and running::False exists in O-RU. 19 
- Software Download has been completed successfully and files are available in O-RU. 20 
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive install-event notifications. 21 
Post-condition: 22 
- O-RU software is installed in the specified target software-slot. 23 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          59 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Figure 12 Software install call flow 2 
NETCONF software-install rpc is used to install the previously downloaded software (all files provided in the package) to the 3 
specified target software-slot on O-RU. This slot must have status active::False and running::False.  4 
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 5 
a) STARTED – software install operation has been started. 6 
b) FAILED – software install operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message. 7 
When O-RU completes the software install or software install procedure fails, the O-RU will send the install-event notification 8 
with one of the following statuses: 9 
a) COMPLETED - Install procedure is successfully completed. 10 
b) FILE_ERROR – operation on the file resulted in in error, disk failure, not enough disk space, incompatible file format 11 
c) INTEGRITY_ERROR – file is corrupted  12 
d) APPLICATION_ERROR – operation failed due to internal reason 13 
When the software install commences, the O-RU shall set the slot status to INVALID. After the install procedure finishes, the 14 
O-RU shall change the slot status to its appropriate status. This operation avoids reporting of inaccurate status when the install 15 
procedure is in operation or when it is interrupted (e.g., by spurious reset operation). 16 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          60 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
5.5 Activation 1 
Pre-condition:  2 
- M-Plane NETCONF session established. 3 
- Software slot to be activated has status VALID. 4 
- O-RU Controller has subscribed to receive activation-event notifications. 5 
Post-condition: 6 
- O-RU software activates to the version of software-slot. 7 
 8 
Figure 13 Software activation call flow. 9 
NETCONF software-activate rpc is used to activate the software. The name of the software -slot is specified in the activate 10 
request.  11 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          61 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
The O-RU shall send an immediate rpc-reply message with one of following statuses: 1 
a) STARTED – software activation operation has been started 2 
b) FAILED – software activation operation could not be proceeded, reason for failure in error-message 3 
When the activation is completed , the O-RU shall send the activation-event notification with the status  of activation. The 4 
following status is returned in the the activation-event notifications. 5 
a) COMPLETED - Activation procedure is successfully completed. O-RU must be restarted via NETCONF reset rpc for the 6 
new software to be activated. 7 
b) APPLICATION_ERROR - operation failed due to internal reason 8 
Only one software slot can be active at a ny time. Thus, successful software-activate command will set active::True to the slot 9 
that was provided in the rpc and automatically will set active::False to the previously active slot. 10 
NETCONF reset rpc shall be sent to O-RU to activate to the version of the software -slot. O-RU restarts and performs startup 11 
procedure as described in Chapter 3 as regular startup with new software version running.  12 
5.6 Software update scenario 13 
An example scenario of a successful software update procedure can be as follows: 14 
1. NETCONF client performs a software inventory operation and identifies that an inactive and not -running slot for  15 
installing software is available so that it can download and install a software package. 16 
NOTE: This version of this specification does not distinguish between a software upgrade and a downgrade. 17 
2. NETCONF client using the software-download rpc requests the O-RU to download a software package (if the 18 
software package contains several files, steps 2-4 need to be performed repeatedly until all files have been downloaded) 19 
3. O-RU sends rpc response that download was started 20 
4. O-RU finishes downloading the file(s) and reports this by sending the download-event notification 21 
5. NETCONF client requests installation of the software using software-install rpc, and provides the slot name where 22 
the software needs to be installed along with a list of filenames to be installed (if the software package contains only 23 
one file, the list will contain only one entry) 24 
6. O-RU sends rpc response that installation was started 25 
7. O-RU sets installation slot status to INVALID 26 
8. O-RU installs the software and after successful install ation (with checksum control) change s status of the slot to 27 
VALID 28 
9. O-RU notifies the notification subscriber that the installation is finished using install-event notification 29 
10. NETCONF client requests the O-RU to activate the newly installed software using the software-activate rpc 30 
11. O-RU sends rpc response that activation was started 31 
12. For requested slot, O-RU changes active to True and at the same time sets activate to False on previously active slot 32 
13. O-RU notifies the notification subscriber about activation finished using the activation-event notification 33 
14. NETCONF client restarts the O-RU forcing it to use the newly installed and activated software into use. O-RU restarts 34 
as regular startup with new software version running. 35 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          62 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
5.7 Factory Reset  1 
O-RU can be reset to the factory default software by activating the software -slot containing the factory default software and 2 
initiating NETCONF reset rpc. O-RU may clear persistent memory data during factory reset as vendor implementation option. 3 
Chapter 6 Configuration Management  4 
6.1 Baseline configuration 5 
This chapter describes NETCONF standard operation (edit-config/get-config/get) [3] which belongs to the CM in Module  to 6 
modify/retrieve any parameters in YANG modules. Examples below use o-ran-hardware as an example YANG module. 7 
Two following scenarios are feasible for Configuration Management purposes. 8 
- 2 phase (modify/commit) operation using writable running datastore 9 
- 3 phase (modify/commit/confirm) operation using candidate datastore. 10 
The 2-phase operation performs edit config on running datastore directly and confirm operation is not used. 11 
All O-RUs shall support 2 phase operation, with 3 phase operations being optional. 12 
6.1.1 Retrieve State 13 
O-RU Controller is able to retrieve state which is defined in o-ran-hardware by using NETCONF <get> procedure: 14 
 15 
Figure 14 – Retrieve Resource State 16

- O-RU Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between O-RU and 18 
O-RU Controllers. 19 
Post conditions: 20 
- O-RU controller has retrieved O-RU state as per <get> request.  21 
6.1.2 Modify State 22 
O-RU Controller is able to change state which can be configurable by using NETCONF <edit-config> procedure without reset. 23

The configurable state are admin-state and power-state defined in o-ran-hardware. 1 
In case of a failure, an error will be returned. Please refer to RFC6241 Appendix A for error codes. 2 
The vendor can define the behavior after the error occurred. 3

 9

- locked: This state indicates that any resource activation is prohibited for the O-RU and all resources have been deactivated 11 
administratively.   12 
- shutting-down: That usage is administratively limited to current instances of use. It's not mandatory (will be optional). 13 
- unlocked: This state indicates that any resource activation is allowed and any resources can be active. The state "unlocked" 14 
is the initial state after the reset of the O-RU. 15

 1 
Figure 17 – Power State 2 
- awake: This state indicates that the O-RU is operating normally, i.e. not in energy saving mode. The state "awake" is the 3 
initial state after the reset of the O-RU. 4 
- sleeping: This state indicates that the O-RU is in energy saving mode. M-plane connection and functions are alive whereas 5 
other C/U/S functions may be stopped to reduce energy consumption. This state is optional. 6 
[oper-state] 7

this case, the O-RU responds <rpc-reply><ok> prior to reset operation. Whatever the previous state is, the O-RU oper-state 9 
starts from disabled when O-RU receives reset. 10

 1 
Figure 20: Availability State 2 
The availability state is derived from detected and active faults and their impact to O-RU’s operation. The availability state is 3 
not affected by faults caused by external reasons.  4 
• normal: There is no fault. 5 
• degraded: When major or critical fault affecting module or any of O-RU’s subcomponents (e.g. transmitter) is active. 6 
• faulty: The critical fault affecting whole O-RU is active and O-RU can't continue any services. 7

idle: No carrier is configured in O-RU. 12

busy: No more carrier can be configured in O-RU. 14 
6.1.3 Retrieve Parameters 15 
O-RU Controller is able to retrieve parameters of the YANG module by using NETCONF <get> or <get-config> procedure 16 
 17 
Figure 22 – Retrieve Parameters 18

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

Preconditions: 1 
- O-RU Controller has completed exchange of NETCONF capabilities as part of connection establishment between O-RU and 2

6.1.4 Modify Parameters 7 
Before an O -RU Controller modifies the configuration (candidate or running) of an O -RU, it shall first lock the target 8 
configuration. This prevents other NETCONF clients from changing the shared config uration database until the O -RU 9 
Controller releases the lock. If another NETCONF client has already locked the configuration datastore, then the O -RU will 10 
respond with a NETCONF error indicating that the requested lock is denied. Note, in such circumstances, the O-RU controller 11 
should wait for a period of time before re-attempting to modify the O-RU’s configuration. 12 
O-RU Controller is able to modify parameters of the YANG module by using the NETCONF <edit-config> procedure. 13 
When supported by an O -RU, the O-RU Controller shall perform any required modify operations ONLY on the candidate 14 
configuration datastore before committing the validated configuration to the running configuration datastore. When an O -RU 15 
does not support the candidate configuration datastore, the O-RU Controller should take extreme care whenever modifying the 16 
running configuration datastore as such will likely impact system operation. 17 
Note, validation of the modified configuration is based on: 18 
1) basic YANG constraints (e.g., min-elements, range, pattern),  19 
2) XPATH based YANG constraints (e.g., leafref, must and when statements), and  20 
3) external code which implements YANG constraints (e.g., defined in O -RAN specifications, YANG description 21 
statements, etc.). 22 
In case of failures, an error will be returned. Please refer to RFC6241 Appendix A for error codes. 23 
The vendor can define the behavior after error occurred. 24

6.1.5 Deleting Parameters 16 
Before an O -RU Controller deletes any configuration (candidate or running) of an O -RU, it shall first lo ck the target 17 
configuration. This prevents other NETCONF clients from changing the shared configuration database until the O -RU 18 
Controller releases the lock. If another NETCONF client has already locked the configuration datastore, then the O -RU will 19 
respond with a NETCONF error indicating that the requested lock is denied. Note, in such circumstances, the O-RU controller 20 
should wait for a period of time before re-attempting to delete the O-RU’s configuration. 21 
O-RU Controller is able to delete parameters of the YANG module by using the NETCONF <edit-config> procedure with the 22 
“operation” attribute set to delete. 23

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
If the configuration data does not exist, an <rpc-error> element is returned with an <error-tag> value of "data-missing". 1 
When support ed by an O -RU, the O -RU Controller shall perform any required delete operations ONLY on the candidate 2 
configuration datastore before committing the validated configuration to the running configuration datastore. When an O -RU 3 
does not support the candidate configuration datastore, the O-RU Controller should take extreme care whenever modifying the 4 
running configuration datastore as such will likely impact system operation. 5

6.2 Framework for optional feature handling 1 
This section describes the common and optional features about Configuration Management. 2 
An O-RU may have some features which are not supported by other O -RUs, i.e. optional feature(s). In this case, the O -RU 3 
needs to inform the O-RU controller which features the O-RU can provide, and this can be achieved by exchanging NETCONF 4 
capabilities. 5 
Some of the YANG models are optional for the O -RU to support. For example, in this version of the management plane 6 
specification, those models associated with External IO and Antenna Line Devices are not essential for the operation of the O-7 
RAN fronthaul interface. Other mandatory models define optional feature capabilities. 8 
Both t he NETCONF Server and NETCONF Client shall use the ietf -yang-library model (RFC 7895) [20] to signal the 9 
namespaces of the models supported by the NETCONF Server. If an O-RU/NETCONF Server does not return the namespace 10 
associated with an optional YANG model, the NETCONF Client determines that the O-RU/NETCONF Server does not support 11 
the optional capability associated with the model. 12 
In addition, for each supported schema, the ietf-yang-library lists the YANG feature names from this module that are supported 13 
by the server. The details of optional models and features are defined in Annex C. 14 
6.3 M-Plane Operational State 15 
The o-ran-mplane-int YANG model allows the O-RU to report the connectivity to NETCONF clients on a per sub -interface 16 
level. The client information includes the IP address(es) for the client(s) as well as the link-layer address used to forward packets 17 
towards the various management plane clients. 18 
6.4 Notification of Updates to Configuration Datastore 19 
6.4.1 Introduction 20 
This sub-section defines an optional O-RU capability which allows O-RU Controllers to configure the O-RU to provide 21 
notifications of modifications to its YANG datastore. This capability can be used when the O-RU is operating in a hybrid 22 
environment with multiple simultaneous NETCONF sessions established to different O-RU controllers. Using this capability, 23 
one particular O-RU controller uses the NETCONF notifications functionality specified in RFC 6470 [35] to enable it to be 24 
automatically signalled changes to the O-RU’s configuration made by a second O-RU controller. Additionally, if the O-RU 25 
supports a vendor specific interface to allow manual configuration, this functionality can also be used to signal such 26 
configuration modifications to an O-RU Controller. 27 
6.4.2 Subscribing to updates from an O-RU 28 
When an O-DU receives an indication from an O-RU that it supports the optional capability to support notification of updates 29 
to its configuration data store, as a minimum, it shall subscribe to the netconf-config-change notification. 30 
An example subscription to the event notification stream is shown in the figure below, where one O-RU Controller is 31 
receiving a notification that the configuration of the O-RU’s timezone offset has been modified by a second O-RU controller.  32

Chapter 7 Performance Management 3 
This chapter provides the description of scenarios related to performance management. It consists of 2 functions. One is for the 4 
measurement activation and the other is the collection of measurement results. 5 
7.1 Measurement Activation and De-activation 6 
The measurement activation at the start-up installation is also allowed as described in chapter 3.  7 
Pre-condition:  8 
M-Plane is operational.  9 
Post-condition: 10 
Measurement is activated or deactivated as per NETCONF client’s request. 11 
This sub -section provides information about how to acti vate and de-activate the performance measurement via NETCONF 12 
<edit-config> to O-RU. The performance measurement is defined as o-ran-performance-management YANG module. In case 13 
of multiple NETCONF clients, only one NETCONF client shall activate/deactivate the measurements in the O-RU. 14 
In the performance-management YANG module, the following parameters are defined. 15 
- group of the measurement results, e.g., transceiver-measurement-objects, rx-window-measurement-objects, tx-16 
measurement-objects, epe-measurement-objects and symbol-rssi-measurement-objects. 17 
- measurement-interval: measurement interval for the measurement-objects to measure the performance periodically, 18 
e.g., 300, 600, 900 seconds. It is defined per the group of the measurement result. 19 
- measurement-object: target metric to measure the performance, e.g., RX_POWER, TX_POWER , defined  as key 20 
parameter. 21 
- active: enable/disable the performance measurement per measurement-object. This va lue is Boolean.  Default is 22 
FALSE. 23 
- start-time and end-time: to report the time of measurement start and end for the measurement-object at each 24 
measurement-interval. 25 
- object-unit: unit to measure the performance per object, e.g., O-RU, physical port number, antenna, carrier. The object-26 
unit may be configurable  Identifier object-unit-id means e.g., physical port number when object unit set to physical 27 
port number. 28 
<notification xmlns="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:notification:1.0"> 
  <eventTime>2020-03-01T08:00:14.12Z</eventTime> 
  <netconf-config-change xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-netconf-
notifications"> 
    <id>102</id> 
    <changed-by> 
      <username>nms-user</username>

- report-info: th e reporting info to the measurement-object, e.g., MAXIMUM, MINIMUM, FIRST, LATEST, 1 
FREQUENCY_TABLE and COUNT. Multiple info can be considered for one object if necessary. 2 
- Optional configurable parameter(s) for report-info: some configurable parameters to report, e.g., function, bin-count, 3 
upper-bound, lower-bound. For the bin-count configuration, it shall be less than the parameter max-bin-count that is 4 
the capability information of NETCONF server for the maximum configurable value for bin-count. 5 
- Additional reporting information for report-info: some additional information to report info, e.g., date-and-time. 6 
The detail of the parameters per measurement-object and the group of measurement result are defined in Annex B. 7 
The measurement-interval of measurement-object may be set to common or different values per group of the measurement 8 
result.  9 
It is allowed that the measurement is activated and deactivated at any time. When different parameter measurements have 10 
intervals with a common factor, the O-RU shall synchronize the boundary of these measurements aligned with this factor, 11 
irrespective of when the different measurements are activated. And all of start point s of the measurement-intervals shall be 12 
synchronized to zero o’clock mid-night by using an equation {full seconds (hour, minute and second) modulo ‘measurement-13 
interval’ = 0}, in order to ensure the same start and end of the measurement-intervals between O-RUs. For more detail see 14 
the following illustration. 15 
 16 
Figure 26: synchronization of measurement-interval. 17 
 18 
The modification of the configurable parameters for the measurement shall be allowed  while active for the corresponding 19 
measurement-object is set to FALSE. 20 
All of the measurements are optionally supported in the O-RU.  21 
The report-info, e.g., count, shall be started from 0 at the boundary of every measurement-interval. No accumulation is 22 
applied between the measurement-intervals. 23 
 7.2 Collection and Reporting of Measurement Result 24 
This sub-section provides the description of scenarios used to collect measurement results. There are three options. 25 
1. NETCONF process: Create-subscription from NETCONF client and NETCONF notification from NETCONF server 26 
are used. 27 
2. File Management process: File upload mechanism is used to transfer the measurement file from O-RU to configured 28 
file server(s) that O-RU can reach to. 29 
3. Configured subscription process: Create configured subscription from O-RU as Event-Producer to Event-Collector. 30 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          72 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Methods 1 and 2 are mandatory for the O-RU. Method 3 shall be supported by those O -RUs that support the optional NON-1 
PERSISTENT-MPLANE feature. The method(s) to be used is the matter of NETCONF client. 2 
In case of multiple NETCONF clients and/or Event-Collectors, the O-RU shall report the same notification-based measurement 3 
results to all subscribed NETCONF clients /Event-Collectors, and the O-RU shall upload file-based results to all configured 4 
fileservers. 5 
7.2.1 NETCONF process 6 
This process needs the NETCONF capability: urn:ietf:params:netconf:capability:notification:1.0 7 
1. NETCONF client subscribes to one or more measurement  group(s) and/or measurement-object(s) to collect the 8 
measurement result by sending NETCONF <subscribe-notification> to NETCONF server in the O-RU. In this message, 9 
startTime and stopTime for the notification may be configurable. NETCONF client can configure the notification-interval 10 
in the performance-measurement YANG module.  11 
2.  NETCONF server sends NETCONF notification messages periodically to the client as configured by  the notification-12 
interval. The NETCONF notification message contains subscribed measurement group(s) and/or measurement-object(s). 13 
The notification-interval doesn’t need to be same as the measurement-interval. The notification timing different from the 14 
measurement-interval is a matter to O-RU implementation. 15 
This procedure is described in the following figure. 16

notifications, the appropriate create-subscription message is required. Please refer to section 8.2 for the appropriate example 20 
of create-subscription of multiple notifications. 21 
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall send <close-session> operation from the subscription session. 22 
If NETCONF session is terminated by <kill-session>, the subscribed notification is terminated as well.  23

When notification-interval is larger than measurement-interval, O-RUs implementing v07.00 or later of this specification 3 
may use a single notification that contains multiple stats included in the list such as multiple-transceiver-measurement-result, 4 
multiple-rx-window-measurement-result, multiple-tx-measurement-result, multiple-epe-measurement-result or 5 
multiple-symbol-rssi-measurement-result which have consecutive periods indicating start-time and end-time for the 6 
measurement. 7 
Note, when multiple measurements stats corresponding to the same measurement -group are available in an O -RU that 8 
implements an earlier version of this specification, the O-RU is only able to include a single statistic in the notification. 9 
In such circumstances, the O-RU should report the latest available statistic in the notification.  10 
Note, an O-RU Controller that implements an earlier version of this specification should ensure that the configuration  11 
of notification-interval and measurement-interval results in only a single measurement statistic corresponding to a 12 
specific measurement-group being reported by the O -RU in any one notification.  In other cases, the O -RU Controller 13 
can use the rules defined in section 1.6 to ignore the newly introduced schema -nodes for reporting multiple 14 
measurements. 15 
When notification-interval is smaller than measurement-interval, one notification may not contain the stats which start-time 16 
and end-time are not applicable to the period for the notification. 17 
For example, when notification-interval = 60min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 18 
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains 2 measurement results for 19 
measurement-object#A with consecutive start-time and end-time, and 4 measurement results for measurement-object#B 20 
with consecutive start-time and end-time.  21 
For the other example, when notification-interval = 15min, measurement-interval for measurement-object#A= 30min and 22 
measurement-interval for measurement-object#B = 15min, one notification contains one measurement results for 23 
measurement-object#B but not for measurement-object#A. next notification contains both measurements result for 24 
measurement-object#A and #B. 25 
7.2.2 File Management process 26 
NETCONF client needs to configure a parameter of performance measurement YANG module ‘enable-file-upload’ to enable 27 
or disable the periodic file upload mechanism via NETCONF <edit-config>. Its default is FALSE. 28 
In addition, the performance measurement YANG module defines file-upload-interval, remote-file-upload-path, credentials 29 
information of the file server and enable-random-file-upload as configurable parameters. 30 
Following types of authentications shall be supported for performance file upload: 31 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          74 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 1 
Following types of authentications may be supported for performance file upload:  2 
 3 
b) X.509 Certificate for FTPES client (O-RU) and FTPES server  4 
c) Certificate for both O-RU and sFTP server authentication 5 
When the parameter enable-file-upload is set to TRUE, O-RU shall store the performance measurement files in the generic 6 
folder in O-RU, i.e., O-RAN/PM/. Every file-upload-interval, O-RU pushes the latest file to upload to the remote-file-upload-7 
path of the configured SFTP/FTPES servers if enable-file-upload is set to TRUE. Otherwise, the performance measurement 8 
file is not created and uploaded. The O-RU shall use the URI scheme of the remote-file-path leaf to determine whether to use 9 
sFTP or FTPES for the file upload. The number of maximum performance files to be stored in O-RU simultaneously is a matter 10 
for O-RU implementation. The O-RU shall manage its own storage space by deleting the older files autonomously.  11 
Note, an O-RU Controller shall only trigger file upload using FTPES if it is using NETCONF/TLS to configure the O-12 
RU 13 
 14 
The O-RU shall ensure that the start-time and the  end-time within the name of the performance measurement file are 15 
synchronized with the same manner as measurement-interval by using file-upload-interval. 16 
If the parameter enable-random-file-upload is set to TRUE, the O-RU shall randomize the timing to upload SFTP or FTPES 17 
file after the performance measurement file is ready to upload. The randomized timing is an O-RU implementation matter and 18 
shall not be later than next file-upload-interval. 19 
The file name of the performance measurement is: 20 
C<start-time>_<end-time>_<name>.csv 21 
- Starting with a capital letter “C”. 22 
- Format of <start-time> and <end-time> can be local time or UTC. 23 
Local time format is YYYYMMDDHHMM+HHMM, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute, timezone “+” or “ -“, 24 
hour and minute for the time zone. 25 
UTC format is YYYYMMDDHHMMZ, indicating, year, month, day, hour, minute and with a special UTC designator 26 
("Z")   27 
Time zone offset is provided by timezone-utc-offset in o-ran-operation.yang. 28 
- <name> in ietf-hardware is used  29 
- “_” underscore is located between <start-time>, <end-time> and <name> 30 
- File extension is “csv” as csv format file. 31 
Example of measurement file is: 32 
C201805181300+0900_201805181330+0900_ABC0123456.csv. 33 
The file format of the performance measurement has following rule: 34 
1. Each line starts with the measurement-object identifier, which measurement can be switched to TRUE or FALSE by 35 
active parameter. The identifier of each measurement-object is defined in Annex B. 36 
2. After the measurement-object identifier, the name of measurement-object, start-time, end-time are followed. 37 
3. Since the report-info results of any measurement-object are measured per object-unit, object-unit-id and set of report-38 
info are repeated in one line. 39 
4. When multiple report-info parameters exist per object-unit, all of the report-info are consecutively listed until the next 40 
object-unit-id. The order of parameters, such as object -unit-id, report-info and additional information for the report-info, 41 
shall be same as the order of those listed in NETCONF notification defined in o-ran-performance-management YANG 42 
module. 43

The performance measurement files stored in O-RAN/PM can be uploaded on-demand. For the file upload mechanism by on-1
