7.2.3 Configured Subscription Process 3 
This optional process requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 4 
process follows the NETCONF process described in sub -section 7.2.1. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <cr eate-5 
subscription > to the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the measurement-result-stats notifications, the NETCONF 6 
client installs the subscription via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends 7 
asynchronous YANG notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 8 
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the corresponding configuration in the O -RU. 9 
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification 10 
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  11 
Note, unlike the NETCONF process described in section 7.2.1, the subscription to the subscribed notifications is not terminated 12 
when the NETCONF session used to establish the subscription is terminated.  13 
Chapter 8 Fault Management 14 
Fault management is responsible for  sending alarm notifications to the configured subscriber, which will typically be the 15 
NETCONF Client  unless the O -RU supports the configured subscription capability, as described in Chapter 15, when the 16 
configured subscriber may be an Event-Collector. FM contains Fault Management Managed Element and via this Managed 17 
Element alarm notifications can be disabled or enabled. 18 
The NETCONF Server is responsible for managing an “active -alarm-list”. Alarms with severity “warning” are excluded from 19 
this list. When an alarm is detected it is added to the list; when the alarm reason disappears then the alarm is cleared - removed 20 
from the “active-alarm-list”. Furthermore, when the element that was the “fault -source” of an alarm is deleted then all related 21 
alarms are removed from the “active-alarm-list”. 22 
The NETCONF Client can read “active-alarm-list” by get rpc operation. 23 
 24 
Figure 29: Read Active Alarms 25 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          77 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
8.1 Alarm Notification 1 
The O-RU is responsible to send <alarm -notif> to a configured subscriber when the NETCONF Client has established a 2 
subscription to alarm notification and: 3 
- a new alarm is detected (this can be the same alarm as an already existing one, but reported against a different “fault-source” 4 
than the existing alarm)  5 
- an alarm is removed from the list   6 
Removal of alarms from the list due to deletion of “fault-source” element is considered as clearing and cause sending of <alarm-7 
notif> to the configured subscriber. This applies to alarms which were explicitly related to the deleted “fault-source” element. 8 
The rationale for such is to avoid misalignment between NETCONF Clients when one NETCONF Client deletes an element.  9 
The O-RU reports in <alarm-notif> only for new active or cancelled alarms, not all active alarms. 10 
 11 
Figure 30: Alarm Notification 12 
8.2 Manage Alarms Request to NETCONF Clients 13 
The NETCONF Client can “subscribe” to Fault Management Element by sending create-subscription, RFC5277 [21], to 14 
NETCONF Server. 15 
RFC5277 allows <create-subscription> below: 16 
        <netconf:rpc netconf:message-id="101" 17 
                xmlns:netconf="urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:base:1.0"> 18 
          <create-subscription 19

            <filter netconf:type="subtree"> 21 
              <event xmlns="http://example.com/event/1.0"> 22 
                <eventClass>fault</eventClass> 23 
                <severity>critical</severity> 24

8.3 Fault Sources 6 
Alarm notifications reported by NETCONF Server contain element “fault -source” which indicates the origin of an alarm. In 7 
general values of “fault-source” are based on names defined as YANG leafs: 8 
- Source (Examples: fan, module, PA, port) 9 
indicates that origin of the alarm within the O-RU. Value of “fault-source” is based on element name. 10 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          80 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Note: In case the NETCONF Server reports an unknown “fault-source”, the NETCONF Client can discard the <alarm-1 
notif>. 2 
- Source (other than when an element is within the O-RU) 3 
Value of fault-source may be empty or may identify the most likely external candidate; for example, antenna line.   4 
 5 
Alarms with different “fault-id”, “fault-source” or "fault-severity" are independent: 6 
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-id” may be reported with different “fault-source”.  7 
- Multiple alarms with same “fault-source” may be reported with different “fault-id”.  8 
- When an alarm with a "fault -id" and a "fault-source" is reported with a "fault -severity" and its severity of alarm condition 9 
is upgraded or degraded, NETCONF server reports a new alarm with the same "fault -id" and the same "fault-source" with 10 
the upgraded or degraded "fault -severity" with "is -cleared"::FALSE and clears the previous alarm with the report of the 11 
"fault-id", "fault-source" and "fault-severity" with "is-cleared":: TRUE.  12 
The range of "fault-id" is separated to c ommon and vendor specific. The common fault -ids are defined in Annex A and more 13 
number will be used in future. The vendor specific range for the fault-id shall be [1000 .. 65535]. 14 
Alarm notifications reported by the NETCONF Server contain names of the “affected-objects” which indicate elements affected 15 
by the fault. In case the origin of the alarm is within the O-RU, other elements than “fault-source” which will not work correctly 16 
due to the alarm are reported via “affected -objects”. In case the origin of the fault is outside of the O-RU, the O-RU elements 17 
which will not work correctly due to the fault are reported via “affected-objects”. 18 
8.4 Manage Alarms Request to Event-Collector 19 
This optional capability requires the O-RU to support configured subscriptions, as described in Chapter 15. The structure of the 20 
process follows the process described in sub -section 8.2. However, instead of sending a NETCONF <create -subscription> to 21 
the NETCONF server in the O-RU to subscribe to the alarm-notif notifications, the NETCONF client installs the subscription 22 
via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends asynchronous YANG 23 
notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-Collector. 24 
In order to terminate the subscription, the NETCONF client shall delete the corresponding configuration in the O -RU. 25 
Immediately after the subscription is successfully deleted, the O -RU will send to a subscription state change notification  26 
indicating that the subscription has ended to the Event-Collector.  27 
Chapter 9 File Management 28 
This chapter specifies File Management for the O-RU. Following operations are supported as a File Management. 29 
- upload (see subsection 9.2) 30 
 File upload from O-RU to file server triggered by O-RU Controller. 31 
- retrieve file list (see subsection 9.3) 32 
 O-RU Controller retrieves the file list in O-RU. 33 
- download (see subsection 9.4) 34 
 File download from file server to O-RU triggered by O-RU Controller 35 
Note: file-download has different purpose with software-download specified in subsection 5.3. For example, file-download 36 
can be used for Beamforming configuration in subsection 12.4. 37 
File transfers are done with sFTP or FTPES. Following types of authentications shall be supported for file management: 38 
a) Password for RU authentication and list of public keys (DSA/RSA) for sFTP server authentication 39

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

Following types of authentications may be supported for file management:  1 
 2 
b) X.509 Certificate for FTPES Client (O-RU) and FTPES Server  3 
c) Certificate for both O-RU and sFTP server authentication 4 
Following other sections are related with File Management. 5 
- Subsection 7.2.2: File Management process (can be used for on demand file upload purpose, since subsection 7.2.2 covers 6 
periodic file upload) 7 
- Subsection 11.2: Log Management 8 
- Subsection 12.4: Beamforming Configuration 9 
Note: the file management functions involve the O-RU controller subscribing to receive particular YANG notifications 10 
from the O -RU. All O -RUs support the NETCONF Create-Subscription method, enabling those notifications to be 11 
transported using NETCONF notifications . In addition, those O -RUs that support  the optional NON -PERSISTENT-12 
MPLANE feature, the O-RU Controller can create a configured subscription from the O-RU, enabling those notifications 13 
to be transported over HTTPS to an Event-Collector as described in Chapter 15. 14 
9.1 File System Structure 15 
The file System structure of the O-RU is represented as a logical structure that is used by the file management procedures 16 
defined in the rest of this chapter. If the O-RU’s physical file structure differs from the logical file structure defined below, the 17 
O-RU is responsible for performing the mapping between the two structures. 18 
The O-RU shall support the standardized logical folders. In this version of the M-Plane specification, the following standardized 19 
folders are defined: 20 
O-RAN/log/ 21 
O-RAN/PM/ 22 
O-RAN/transceiver/ 23 
And for those O-RU’s supporting beamforming 24 
O-RAN/beamforming/ 25 
The O-RU may additionally support vendor defined folders which are out of scope of this specification. 26 
9.2 File Management Operation: upload 27 
This subsection describes file upload method from O-RU to the fileserver. sFTP or FTPES is used for File management, and 28 
one file can be uploaded by one upload operation. The O-RU Controller triggers file upload operation to O-RU. 29 
Simultaneous multiple file upload operations can be supported under the same FTP connection between O-RU to the fileserver. 30 
If the O-RU has the number of limitation to upload simultaneously as a capability, it is allowed that O-RU reports failure 31 
notification for the upload request which is larger than the capability. The behaviour of O-RU Controller is out of scope when 32 
O-RU Controller receives failure notification from the O-RU. 33 
Following rpc is used for upload operation. 34 
-rpc: file-upload 35 
-  input 36 
-  local-logical-file-path: the logical path of file to be uploaded (no wildcard is allowed) 37 
-  remote-file-path: URI of file on the fileserver 38 
-  output 39 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          82 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
-  status: whether O-RU accepted or rejected the upload request  1 
-  reject-reason: the human readable reason why O-RU rejects the request (only applicable if status is rejected) 2 
In the rpc-reply, status whether the O-RU receives the upload request or rejects due to some reason (e.g., the number of 3 
limitation to upload simultaneously) is replied. If rejected, the human readable reject reason is also replied. 4 
In notification, the result of the upload process (successfully uploaded or failed upload) is replied in addition to local -logical-5 
file-path and remote-file-path. If failure, the human readable reason is also replied.  The figure below shows the file upload 6

Chapter 10 Synchronization Aspects 1 
This chapter provides the Management Plane’s interactions with various aspects of the time synchronization of the O-RU. In 2 
general, the O-RU is responsible for managing its synchronization status, to select one or more synchronization input source(s) 3 
(based on vendor specific implementation)  and assure that the resulting accuracy meets that required by the R adio Access 4 
Technology being implemented. 5 
10.1 Sync Status Object 6 
This sync container provides synchronization state of the module. If the O-RU Controller is interested in Sync status, it may 7 
configure a subscription to the synchronization-state-change notification in the O-RU.  Event notifications will be sent 8 
whenever the state of the O-RU synchronization changes. 9 
The State of O-RU synchronization is indicated by the following allowed values: 10 
- LOCKED: O-RU is in the locked mode, as defined in ITU-T G.810.  11 
- HOLDOVER: O-RU clock is in holdover mode. 12 
- FREERUN: O-RU clock isn’t locked to an input reference and is not in the holdover mode. 13 
The sync container allows the O-RU to list via an array the synchronization sources which it is capable of supporting.   The 14 
allowed values are: 15 
• GNSS 16 
• PTP 17 
• SYNCE 18 
 19 
Figure 36: Allowed sync state transitions 20 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          86 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Note: HOLDOVER mode is optional and depends on internal O-RU design. 1 
10.2 Sync Capability Object 2 
The module’s synchronization capability is provided via this object.  This indicates the accuracy o f the derived Telecom 3 
Subordinate Clock (T-TSC) to which the module’s design is capable of. For details on the actual capability levels, see section 4 
9.3 of the O-RAN WG4 CUS plane specification [2]. There are two enumerations possible: 5 
• CLASS_B 6 
• ENHANCED 7 
10.3 PTP Configuration 8 
This container defines the configuration of Precision Time Protocol.   9 
domain-number 10 
This parameter indicates the Domain Number for PTP announce messages. Allowed values: 0 ~ 255. 11 
Default: 24. 12 
Note: ITU-T G.8275.1 [22] uses domain numbers in the range 24...43, but the entire range is allowed to ensure flexibility 13 
of the M-Plane specification. For ITU-T G.8275.2 domain numbers from range 44…63 shall be used. 14 
accepted-clock-classes 15 
Contains the list of PTP acceptable Clock Classes, sorted in the descending order. 16 
Note: The sender must generate the list of acceptable clock classes. The list must be sorted in descending order. Each accepted 17 
Clock Class value must appear only once in the list. Depending on implementation, the receiver may interpret the list in either 18 
of two ways: 19 
a) use only the first (i.e. the maximum) item in the list, interpreting it as a threshold value for acceptable clock classes, 20 
while ignoring all other items in the list; 21 
b) use the whole list, interpreting it as an explicit list of acceptable clock classes. 22 
Default: 7, 6 23 
clock-class 24 
The PTP Clock Class accepted by the O-RU. Allowed values: 0 ~ 255. 25 
Note: Not all values are compliant to [22], but the entire range is allowed in M-plane specification to ensure flexibility. The 26 
values can be validated/filtered on the receiver side, if necessary. 27 
ptp-profile 28 
Defines which PTP profile will be used. 29 
Allowed values: 30 
• G_8275_1 (multicast over Ethernet will be used, see: ITU-T G.8275.1) 31 
• G_8275_2 (unicast over IP will be used, see: ITU-T G.8275.2) 32 
Default: G_8275_1. 33 
delay-asymmetry 34 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          87 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Defines the static phase error in the recovered PTP timing signal to be compensated at the O-DU. The error is defined in units 1 
of nanoseconds in the range ±10 000 ns. According to ITU-T G.810 [23] and IEEE1588 [24] and [50], the sign of the parameter 2 
is interpreted as follows: 3 
• If the phase error to be compensated is negative, then the recovered timing signal shall be advanced by the time interval 4 
equal to the configured value to compensate the error. 5 
• If the phase error to be compensated is positive, then the recovered timing signal shall be delayed by the time interval 6 
equal to the configured value to compensate the error. 7 
Default: 0 8 
Note: Modification of this parameter may have impact on RF transmission, but shall occur without unit restart. 9 
Note: This parameter is optional for support. If the O-RU does not support this value, the O-RU uses the default value. If the 10 
O-RU does not support manual compensation, it ignores the parameter setting. 11 
Note: Granularity of the applied value depends on the architecture and implementation of the system clock, and therefore, may 12 
vary across vendors. 13 
10.3.1 G.8275.1 specific parameters 14 
multicast-mac -address 15 
The parameter defines the destination MAC address, used by the O-RU in the egress PTP messages. 16 
Allowed values: 17 
• FORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-1B-19-00-00-00  destination MAC address) 18 
• NONFORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-80-C2-00-00-0E  destination MAC address) 19 
Default value: FORWARDABLE. 20 
10.3.2 G.8275.2 specific parameters 21 
This section contains G.8275.2 specific parameters 22 
local-ip-port 23 
The parameter defines local ip address which will be used as a port for receiving ptp signal 24 
master-ip-configuration 25 
The parameter defines list of ip configuration of devices acting as ptp signal source. 26 
local-priority 27 
The parameter defines local priority or underlying master IP address. 28 
ip-address 29 
the parameter defines master IP address. 30 
log-inter-sync-period 31 
The parameter defines number of sync message during 1 second 32 
Allowed values: 0 ~ -7 (this represents the value from 1 message per second to 128 messages per second) 33 
log-inter-announce-period 34 
The parameter defines number of announce message during 1 second 35 
Allowed values: 0 ~ -3 (this represents the value from 1 message per second to 8 messages per second) 36 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          88 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
10.4 PTP Status 1 
The PTP Status container is used to collect operational status information of the PTP ordinary clock, controlled by the O-RU. 2 
The object may be used to display operational inf ormation, which facilitates troubleshooting, to the operator. The information 3 
in the object shall not be used by the O-DU to autonomously alter its operation. If  the O-RU Controller is interested in PTP 4 
status, it may configure a subscription to the ptp-state-change notification in the O-RU. Notifications will only indicate changes 5 
to the lock -state.  B efore requesting or subscribing to PTP status information, the O-RU Controller shall ensure that PTP is 6 
supported by the O-RU by requesting the supported-timing-reference-types, as defined in this chapter ( Section 10.1). The 7 
following list includes the related parameters of this container. 8 
reporting-period 9 
This parameter defines minimum period in seconds between reports, sent by the O-RU, for parameters in this container. 10 
default: 10 11 
lock-state 12 
This parameter indicates whether the integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP flow. The 13 
exact definition when to indicate locked or unlocked is up to specific implementation. 14 
• LOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP flow. 15 
• UNLOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is not synchronizing to the reference, recovered from PTP flow. 16 
clock-class 17 
This parameter contains the clock class of the clock, controlled by the O-RU. 18 
sources 19 
This parameter contains characteristics of PTP sources of the clock, controlled by the O-RU. 20 
state 21 
This parameter indicates status of the PTP source: 22 
• PARENT: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source is currently used as a synchronization reference. 23 
• OK: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source can be potentially used as a synchronization reference, i.e. 24 
Announce messages, received from this source, contain acceptable content (domain number, clockclass, flags, etc). 25 
• NOK: Indicates that the PTP signal from this source cannot be used as a synchronization reference, i.e. Announce 26 
messages, received from this source, contain unacceptable content (domain number, clockclass, flags, etc). 27 
• DISABLED: Indicates that PTP connection is not available from this PTP source. 28 
See the related o-ran-sync YANG Model for the full details. 29

This container defines the configuration of SyncE 31 
acceptance-list-of-ssm 32 
The parameter contains the list of SyncE acceptable Synchronization Status Messages (SSM). 33 
Allowed values: 34 
• PRC (Primary Reference Clock) 35 
• PRS (Primary Reference Source-Stratum 1) 36 
• SSU_A (Synchronisation Supply Unit A) 37

• ST2 (Stratum 2) 2 
• ST3 (Stratum 3) 3 
• ST3E (Stratum 3E) 4 
• EEC1 (Ethernet Equipment Clock 1) 5 
• EEC2 (Ethernet Equipment Clock 2) 6 
• DNU (Do Not Use) 7 
• NONE 8 
ssm-timeout 9 
The parameter contains the value of maximum duration in seconds for which the actual SSM value may be different than 10 
configured values. 11

the O-RU. Notifications will only indicate changes to the lock -state.  Before requesting or subscribing to SyncE status 15

reporting-period 18

default: 10 20 
lock-state 21 
This parameter indicates, whether the integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from the SyncE 22 
signal. The exact definition when to indicate locked or unlocked is up to specific implementation. 23 
• LOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is synchronizing to the reference, recovered from the SyncE signal. 24 
• UNLOCKED: The integrated ordinary clock is not synchronizing to the reference, recovered from the SyncE signal. 25 
sources 26 
This parameter contains characteristics of SyncE sources of the clock, controlled by the NETCONF Server 27 
state 28 
This parameter indicates status of the SyncE source: 29 
• PARENT: Indicates that the SyncE signal from this source is currently used as a synchronization reference. 30 
• OK: Indicates that the SyncE signal from this source can be potentially used as a synchronization reference, i.e. SSM 31 
messages, received from this source, contain acceptable clock quality level. 32 
• NOK: Indicates that the SyncE signal from this source cannot be used as a synchroniz ation reference, i.e. SSM 33 
messages, received from this source, contain unacceptable clock quality level. 34 
• DISABLED: Indicates that SSMs are not received from this SyncE source. 35 
quality-level 36 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          90 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
This parameter contains value of the SSM clock quality level, received in SSM messages from the SyncE source. 1 
See the related o-ran-sync YANG Model for the full details. 2 
10.7 GNSS Configuration 3 
This container defines the configuration of Global Navigation Satellite System (GNSS). 4 
enable 5 
This parameter defines if GNSS receiver shall be enabled or not. Allowed values: true/false; 6 
Default values: false. 7 
satellite-constellation-list 8 
This parameter defines list of constellations to be used to acquire synchronization. 9 
Allowed values: 10 
• GPS 11 
• GLONASS 12 
• GALILEO 13 
• BEIDOU 14 
polarity 15 
This parameter defines pulse polarity 16 
Allowed values: 17 
• POSITIVE 18 
• NEGATIVE 19 
Default value: POSITIVE. 20 
cable-delay 21 
This parameter is used to compensate cable delay. Allowed values: 0 ~ 1000 22 
Default value: 5 23 
Note: This value is given in ns (nanoseconds) it is recommended to compensate 5ns per each meter of the cable. 24 
anti-jam-enable {if feature GNSS-ANTI-JAM} 25 
This parameter is used to enable or disable anti-jamming. Allowed values: true/false 26 
Default value: false. 27 
10.8 GNSS Status 28 
An O-RU supporting GNSS capability uses the gnss-state container to report the state of its GNSS receiver. If the O-RU 29 
Controller is interested in GNSS status, it may configure a subscription to the gnss-state-change notification in the O-RU 30 
before requesting or subscribing the GNSS status information. Notifications will only provide changes to the gnss-status. The 31 
O-RU Controller shall ensure that GNSS is supported by the O-RU by requesting supported timing reference types, as defined 32 
in this chapter (Section 10.1). The following list summarizes the related parameters of this container. 33 
gnss-status  34 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          91 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
This parameter indicates the status of the GNSS receiver: 1 
• SYNCHRONIZED: Indicates that the GNSS receiver is synchronized. 2 
• ACQUIRING-SYNC: Indicates the GNSS receiver is functioning correctly, but has not acquired synchronization 3 
• ANTENNA-DISCONNECTED: Indicates the GNSS receiver is reporting that its antenna is disconnected. 4 
• INITIALIZING: Indicates that the GNSS receiver is initializing. 5 
• ANTENNA-SHORT-CIRCUIT: Indicates that the GNSS receiver is reporting that its antenna is short circuited. 6 
Additionally, when the GNSS receiver is synchronized, the O-RU can report the following additional information: 7 
satellites-tracked 8 
The number of satellites being tracked by the O-RU receiver 9 
altitude, latitude and longitude 10 
The geospatial location reported by the GNSS receiver 11 
Chapter 11 Operations Use Cases 12 
11.1 Supervision  Failure Handling and Supervision Termination 13 
Handling 14 
This sub-section clarifies Supervision Failure Handling and Supervision Termination Handling.  15 
11.1.1 Supervision Failure handling 16 
When Supervision Failure is detected by O-RU, the O-RU immediately disables operation of the watchdog timers for the 17 
corresponding NETCONF session. O-RU assumes NETCONF session related to failed supervision is no longer valid. O-RU 18 
terminates this invalid NETCONF session by closing underlying SSH or TLS connection. Then O-RU starts performing the 19 
call home procedure towards the NETCONF client, using the re-call-home-no-ssh-timer to repeat the call home attempts. 20 
This activity is repeated by the O-RU until, either: 21 
 22 
- New NETCONF session is established by the original NETCONF client, or 23 
- The original NETCONF client is no longer a “known O-RU Controller” as defined in sub-section 3.2, e.g., 24 
when reperforming DHCP configuration, the O-RU Controller identity corresponding to the NETCONF client 25 
is no longer signaled by the DHCP server, and/or the NETCONF client was previously configured using the 26 
configured-client-info container and this configuration has been deleted.  27 
 28 
Case #1:  After entering Supervision Failure handling, the O-RU is still having at least one running and valid NETCONF 29 
session with a NETCONF client that has subscribed to receive the supervision-notification. 30 
 31 
The O-RU remains operational and performs periodical Call Home towards known O-RU controllers as 32 
described in sub-section 3.2. 33 
 34 
Case #2:  After entering Supervision Failure handling, the O-RU does not have running NETCONF session with any 35 
NETCONF client that has subscribed to receive the supervision-notification.  36 
The O-RU ceases all radio transmission and performs autonomous reset. 37 
11.1.2 Supervision Termination handling  38 
If NETCONF session used for the supervision subscription is terminated by NETCONF client, the O-RU disables operation 39 
of the watchdog timers for terminated NETCONF session and starts performing Call Home procedure towards known O-RU 40 
Controllers, following specification in sub-section 3.2.  41 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          92 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Before terminating its NETCONF session, a NETCONF client that has subscribed to receive supervision notification, should 2 
at least de-activate all carriers previously configured by this NETCONF client. Optionally, such a NETCONF client can also 3 
remove (full or partial) configuration applied by this NETCONF client to the O-RU. 4 
In case when entering Supervision Termination handling, the O-RU does not have running NETCONF session with any 5 
NETCONF client that has subscribed to receive the supervision-notification, the O-RU ceases all radio transmission. 6 
11.2 Log management 7 
There are two type of log managements, troubleshooting log and trace log. They are independent each other. 8 
Troubleshooting log file contains the logs continuously collected before <start -troubleshooting-logs> rpc. Any logs collected 9 
after <start-troubleshooting-logs> rpc are not contained. 10 
Trace log file contains the logs continuously collected after <start-trace-logs> rpc. Any logs collected before <start-trace-logs> 11 
rpc are not contained. 12 
11.2.1 Troubleshooting 13 
By requesting technical logs an O-RU controller is able to get  collected log data files that can be used for troubleshooting 14 
purposes.  15 
The O-RU provides all possible troubleshooting log files. The contents and log formats are dependent on O-RU implementation. 16 
The number and size of files provided by O-RU is not restricted but the O-RU may keep the number and size of files reasonably 17 
small to allow completion of the whole “Troubleshooting data upload” scenario (all files) within 15 minutes  (with target to 18 
complete within 3 minutes). It is also recommended to provide more useful files first.  19 
Note, the O-RU controller is free to continue the scenario till completion past the allowed time or skip requesting further files. 20 
The files should be compressed with compression method indicated by file name extension:  21 
• .gz (DEFLATE),  22 
• .lz4 (LZ4),  23 
• .xz (LZMA2 - xz utils),  24 
• .zip (DEFLATE - zlib library). 25 
O-RU shall start collecting the troubleshooting logs.  26 
The rpc <start -troubleshooting-logs> triggers the O -RU to start creating files containing troubleshooting logs. Completed 27 
generation of files is indicated by NETCONF server to NETCONF client in form of a notification. 28 
 29 
Figure 37: Start Creating Troubleshooting Log 30

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
The rpc <stop-troubleshooting-logs> informs O-RU that NETCONF client cancels creating troubleshooting logs files and is no 1 
longer interested in receiving <troubleshooting-log-generated> notification. 2 
 3 
Figure 38: Stop Troubleshooting Log 4 
The notification <troubleshooting-logs-generated> is signalled to the configured subscriber after the O-RU has finished creating 5 
all troubleshooting logs, indicating to the subscriber that the logs are ready to be uploaded.  The O-RU shall include URLs for 6 
all troubleshooting log files in the notification, corresponding to the  troubleshooting logs collected before rpc <start -7 
troubleshooting-logs>.  8 
After notification, the O-RU shall stop sending the further notifications <troubleshooting-logs-generated> for troubleshooting 9 
logs collected after rpc <start-troubleshooting-logs> without the rpc <stop-troubleshooting-logs>. 10

The overall troubleshooting log behaviour is illustrated in the following figure. It contains 2 cases, successful notification case 14 
and no notification as abnormal case. In the successful notification case, the notification provides URLs of files containing  all 15 
troubleshooting logs collected before rpc <start -troubleshooting-logs>. After notification, NETCONF client doesn't need to  16 
signal rpc <stop -troubleshooting-logs> since RU stops creating troubleshooting logs. In the no notification case as one of 17 
abnormal scenarios, NETCONF client can make O -RU cancel creating the log files because O -RU doesn't send a notification 18 
for created log files for a long period. 19

11.2.2 Trace 3 
By requesting trace logs an O-RU controller is able to get collected log data files that can be used for trace purposes.  4 
The O-RU provides all possible trace log files. The contents and log formats are dependent on O-RU implementation. 5 
The files should be compressed with compression method indicated by file name extension. 6 
O-RU shall start collecting the trace logs at the moment of receiving <start-trace-logs> rpc. Notification <trace-log-generated> 7 
shall be periodically send to O-RU controller once collected logs stored in file(s) is(are) ready. URL of newly created log file(s) 8 
shall be included in notification. The number and size of files provided by O-RU in a single <trace-log-generated> notification 9 
is not restricted but the O-RU may keep the number and size of files reasonably small to allow completion of the whole “Trace 10 
data upload” scenario (all files from notification) within 15 minutes (with target to complete within 3 minutes). 11 
Note: Timing of creating trace log files is up to O-RU implementation. 12 
After <stop-trace-logs> rpc received from controller, O -RU is mandated to stop collecting trace logs and to send last <trace -13 
log-generated> notification with the is-notification-last:: TRUE and URL(s) of file(s) which contain log data collected between 14 
previous <trace-log-generated> notification and <stop-trace-logs> rpc.  15 
The file transfer mechanism for the created trace log files shall be handled by the file management described in Chapter 9 Fi le 16 
Management. 17

11.3 Operational aspects of Antenna Line Devices 3 
An O-RU can connect to one or more external equipment such as a RET, MultiRET, MHA, RAE and etc. 4 
For the communication with the external equipment, AISG 2.0 protocol [26] as Layer 7 application and HDLC protocol as 5 
Layer 2 data link are used. 6 
- HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239 ( https://www.iso.org/standard/37010.html). Detailed informati on can 7 
also be found in TS 37.462 [27]. 8 
- AISG 2.0 protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna line devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” [26] which is an 9 
adaptation of Iuant interface application layer defined in TS 37.466 [28].  10 
An O-RU may provide one or more ALD ports supporting connection with Antenna Line Devices. Each ALD port shall be able 11 
to support more than one ALD (i.e., a chained ALD configuration). 12 


                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          96 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
This section describes the communication mechanisms based on AISG 2.0 protocol [26]. Fo r communication with external 1 
equipment, AISG 2.0 uses Application Part protocols (RETAP, TMAAP etc.) at Layer 7 and HDLC as a Layer 2 datalink 2 
protocol. 3 
Note, further definitions of O-RU support for Antenna Line Devices will be included in a future versio n of this specification, 4 
and will target support of the AISG 3.0 protocol. 5 
11.3.1 HDLC Interworking 6 
HDLC protocol is standardized by ISO/IEC 13239. Detailed information can also be found in TS 37.462 [27]. The AISG 2.0 7 
protocol is standardized by “Control interface for antenna line devices Standard No. AISG v2.0” which is an adaptation of Iuant 8 
interface application layer defined in TS 37.466 [28]. 9 
Note: the assumed HDLC communication speed is 9600 bits per second. 10 
In order to handle collision detection in the HDLC branch, an O-RU supporting the ALD functionality shall support the 11 
following running counters reported using the corresponding YANG model: 12 
-  Frames with wrong FCS 13 
-  Frames without stop flag 14 
-  Number of received octets 15 
For running counters served by the O-RU, both the O-RU and NETCONF Client shall handle wrap-over mechanism in a way, 16 
that wrap over zero is not considered as erroneous situation. 17 
A NETCONF client can recover these counters. From the changes observed in above counters, a NETCONF Client can deduce 18 
the presence of a collision on the HDLC bus. Additional diagnostic information may be derived from how these counters are 19 
incrementing. 20 
Additionally, the O-RU implements "RPC Status" to indicate status of last "ald-communication" RPC to requestor. 21 
-  Status - flow control indicator of last requested operation (Status of RPC). 22 
Prior to any communication with ALD(s), the O-RU shall provide ALDs with DC power. The way of how DC power is managed 23 
is out of scope of this interface specification. 24 
In order to support collision detection and flow control, the following reference architecture with functional split is defined: 25

11.3.2 ALD Operations 3 
The NETCONF Client sends RPC <ald-communication> to the O-RU. The RPC has following input parameters: 4 
- leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) - contains the identity of the ALD port. The O-RU shall output the data to (corresponds to O-RU 5 
resources provided to NETCONF Client as inventory information) 6 
- leaf: ald-req-msg (up to 1200 bytes) - may contain HDLC address, control bits and payload (see: TS 37.462 for details) 7 
The O-RU performs HDLC communication with the ALD as follows: immediately after the requested payload is sent to the 8 
ALD over the desired ALD port, the O-RU switches the ALD port into reception mode.  9 
Note, for details of HDLC transmission and reception algorithm, please see TS 37.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing". Bits 10 
received within reception window are formed to octets and inserted as payload into ald-resp-msg. 11 
The O-RU responds to the NETCONF Client using the <rpc-reply> message containing following parameters: 12 
- leaf: ald-port-id (uint8) 13 
- leaf: status 14 
- leaf: ald-resp-msg (up to 1200 bytes) 15 
- leaf: frames-with-wrong-crc (4 bytes) 16 
- leaf: frames-without-stop-flag (4 bytes) 17 
- leaf: number-of-received-octets (4 bytes) 18 
Note: In case there is no response from the ALD received within the reception window, the record "ald-resp-msg" in <rpc-19 
reply> sent by the O-RU shall be empty. 20 
After reception, the O-RU shall wait an additional 3ms befor e the next transmission towards HDLC bus is initiated. See TS 21 
37.462, chapter 4.5 "Message timing" for details. 22 
 23 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          98 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Figure 44: ALD Message Transfer 2 
General scenario 3 
Precondition:  4 
M-Plane connectivity between NETCONF Client and NETCONF Server is successfully established. NETCONF Server reports 5 
presence of the supported HDLC Primary Devices. 6 
 7 
1) NETCONF Client triggers DC voltage on desired ALD ports using NETCONF <edit-config> RPC. After DC is turned on - 8 
NETCONF Client waits 3s. 9 
2) NETCONF Client performs HDLC link speed alignment to assure that all ALDs connected to a particular port have switched 10 
themselves to the correct baud rate used by this port.  11 
3) NETCONF Client performs HDLC bus scan using desired HDLC Primary Device offered by O-RU. 12 
3) NETCONF Client determines presence of HDLC Secondary Devices. 13 
4) NETCONF Client assigns HDLC addresses to desired HDLC Secondary Devices. 14 
5) NETCONF Client initiates HDLC layer for secondary devices by sending SNRM command. 15 
6) NETCONF Client starts polling procedure for every HDLC-addressed Secondary Device. 16 
Postcondition:  17

Detected and addressed HDLC Secondary Devices are available for configuration. 1 
11.4 Operational aspects of external IO 2 
An O-RU can connect to one or more input and output ports for external device supervision and control. 3 
The External IO has the following functions 4 
- INPUT: Supervising external devices 5 
- OUTPUT: Controlling external devices 6 
Also, external IO function include signalling to get the O-RU and O-RU controller in sync, enables port monitoring on the O-7 
RU and provides notification from the O-RU to an O-RU controller, and provides control from an O-RU controller to the O-8 
RU and enables output port controlling on the O-RU.  9 
The O-RU only implements external IO yang module if the O-RU supports External IO aspect. 10 
A change in condition of the external IO shall not affect other O-RU services such as RF transmission / reception behaviour. 11 
11.4.1 External input 12 
This section explains single external input line case. For multiple external inputs case, same behaviour for each input shall  be 13 
processed individually. 14 
For input, the O-RU and O-RU controller shall support two scenarios.  15 
[1] To retrieve input state from O-RU controller and respond the input state from the O-RU to O-RU controller. 16 
[2] To send notification from the O-RU to O-RU controller when input state is changed. 17 
The value shall be 18 
 TRUE: Circuit is open. 19 
 FALSE: Circuit is closed 20 
When nothing is connected to the line the value shall be TRUE. 21

be processed individually. 5 
For output, the O-RU and O-RU controller shall support two scenarios.  6 
[1] To retrieve output state from O-RU controller and respond the output state from the O-RU to O-RU controller.  7 
[2] To send edit-config from the O-RU to O-RU controller when output state change is required. 8

 TRUE: Circuit is open. 10

12.1 Retrieval of O-RU Information 4

as SW Management, U-plane configuration and Performance Management will use these retrieved O-RU information. 6 
The following information, for example, can be retrieved from the O-RU: 7 
hw/hardware/component 8

retrieve product-code – the O-RAN defined product code 13 
o-ran-operations/operational-info/declarations 14

 retrieve supported-cusplane-version – the version of the O-RAN CUS-Plane interface 16

12.2 User plane message routing 6 
The purpose of U -Plane configuration is to define the relationship between U -Plane application endpoints  in the O-DU and 7 
those in the O-RU. After such relationships are defined, the application endpoints are able to exchange IQ data using the U-8 
Plane application protocol defined in [2]. 9 
Precondition: 10 
• M-Plane connectivity is established between NETCONF Client and NETCONF Server 11 
12.2.1 Configurable format for eAxC_ID  12 
The eAxC_ID is used by C/U-plane application  to manage  eCPRI communication between desired  C/U-Plane application 13 
components in O-DU and O-RU. 14 
As defined in [2], the eAxC_ID consists of four parameters: DU-PORT, RU-PORT, CC-ID and BAND-SECTOR-ID. Order of 15 
parameters in eAxC_ID must follow definitions in CUS-Plane spec. In this version of the O-RAN WG4 specification, the length 16 
of eAxC_ID is constant and equal to 16 bits. To enable optimal sharing of the 16 bits between these four parameters, the 17 
assignment of eAxC_ID bits to parameters is not fixed. As a consequence, there is a need for NETCONF client to configure the 18 
bit assignment to parameters mappings using the M-Plane interface. 19 
To handle flexible bit assignment, configurable bitmasks are defined for each parameter.  20 
Note: flexible configuration means, that bits of eAxC_ID can be assigned to parameters in runtime.  21 
Rules to be followed by NETCONF Client when configuring bit assignments: 22 
- notation used for parameters forming eAxC_ID is from the LSB. 23 
- each parameter uses consecutive bits 24 
- each parameter can occupy 0-16 bits 25 
- single bit of eAxC_ID cannot be assigned to more than one parameter 26 
 27 
RPC edit-config shall be used to configure bit assignments to O-RU. 28 
Bit assignment change for parameters related to an existing carrier is not allowed. (Impacted carriers need to be deactivated and 29 
deleted prior to any change in eAxC_ID configuration, and then be subsequently created and activated.) 30 
An example of bit assignment usage where 3 bi ts are assigned to the BAND -SECTOR-ID, 3 bits for CC -ID, 7 bit for DU-31 
PORT-ID and 3 bits for RU-PORT-ID is shown below: 32 
<du-port-bitmask> 1111111000000000 </du-port-bitmask> 33 
<band-sector-bitmask> 0000000111000000 </band-sector-bitmask> 34 
<ccid-bitmask> 0000000000111000 </ccid-bitmask> 35 
<ru-port-bitmask> 0000000000000111 </ru-port-bitmask> 36 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          104 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
12.2.2 U-Plane endpoint addressing 1 
Parameter “eaxc-id” for low-level-tx-endpoint and low-level-rx-endpoint, defined using an unsigned 16 bit integer, shall follow 2 
the eaxc-id addressing schema defined in section 12.2.1 . Please refer to the eaxc -id parameter description in CUS plane 3 
specification [2]. 4 
The NETCONF Client is responsible for assigning unique values to the "eaxc_id" addresses  to all low-level-rx-endpoint 5 
elements and low-level-tx-endpoint elements, within the O-RU when operating in the same direction (Tx or Rx), even when 6 
these operate across different named interfaces of the O-RU. 7 
More precisely, the same eaxc-id cannot be simultaneously assigned to multiple -low-level-rx-endpoints or to multiple and low-8 
level-tx-endpoints. Clarifying eaxc-id assignment by example, and unless otherwise specified, within the same O -RU 9 
(considering a 2 × 2 MIMO): 10 
Case 1: Allowed eaxc-id assignment (same antenna ports used for Tx and Rx) 11 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=1 12 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=1 13 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=2 14 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=2 15 
Case 2: Allowed eaxc-id assignment (separate antenna ports used for Tx and Rx) 16 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=1 17 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=2 18 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=3 19 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=4 20 
 21 
Case 3: Prohibited eaxc-id assignment (separate antenna ports used for Tx and Rx) 22 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=1 23 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 1) – eaxc-id=2 24 
- low-level-rx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=1 25 
- low-level-tx-endpoint (name 2) – eaxc-id=2 26 
 27 
12.2.3 General configuration scenario 28 
Below is described the general scenario to be followed by a NETCONF Client in order to properly configure communication 29 
between C/U-Plane endpoints in the O-DU and O-RU. 30 
All operations can be performed in any order (including combini ng some of them in one request) provided assumed result 31 
(overall configuration) of each request sent by NETCONF Client is valid. Note selected highlighted rules below: 32 
-  eaxc-id is unique for all endpoints within the O-RU in the same direction (Tx or Rx) and linked with any low-level-rx-link or 33 
low-level-tx-link element 34 
-  at the moment of creation, every low-level-rx-link must be linked to an existing rx-array-carrier element and existing 35 
processing-element element  36 
-  at the moment of creation, every low-level-tx-link must be linked to an existing tx-array-carrier element and existing 37 
processing-element element 38 
1) NETCONF Client determines the presence of following elements offered by NETCONF Server: 39 
- tx-arrays  - by fetching the list of tx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 40 
- rx-arrays - by fetching the list of rx-arrays in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 41 
- static_low-level-tx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-tx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 42 
- static_low-level-rx-endpoint elements - by fetching the list static-low-level-rx-endpoints in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 43 
- interface elements - by fetching list of interfaces in o-ran-interfaces.yang 44 

                        
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ          105 
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
2) NETCONF Client determines capabilities exposed by static -low-level-tx-endpoints and static -low-level-rx-endpoints. 1 
Additionally. NETCONF Client determines capabilities exposed by "endpoint-types" and "endpoint-capacity-sharing-groups" 2 
and specific parameters proprietary to [tr]x -array(s). Obtained information must be respected when NETCONF Client 3 
configures low-level-[tr]x-endpoints referenced to static-low-level[tr]x-endpoints by parameter "name". 4 
3) For elements determined in step 1) NETCONF Client examines relationship between  5 
- static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and tx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 6 
- static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and rx-array elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang 7 
- static-low-level-tx-endpoint elements and interface elements 8 
- static-low-level-rx-endpoint elements and interface elements 9 
- tx-arrays, rx-arrays and their elements in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang. 10 
Note: Netconf Client retrieves the content of o-ran-beamforming,yang module to obtain knowledge regarding beamforming -11 
related parameters that apply for particular Netconf Server. This step is optional, as o-ran-beamforming.yang module exists 12 
only in case Netconf Server supports beamforming. Obtained parameters are needed by Netconf Client to perform beamforming 13 
control. 14 
4) For every static-low-level-rx-endpoint NETCONF Client determines endpoint's ability to support non-time managed and/or 15 
time managed traffic.  Information about delayed traffic type supported by endpoints is exposed through parameter managed-16 
delay-support (enumeration) under endpoint -types and it indicates whether the endpoint can support time managed traffic 17 
(MANAGED), non-time managed traffic (NON_MANAGED), or both (BOTH). It is required that the desired type of supported 18 
traffic to be configured to the endpoint. Configuration is assumed to be static for run -time. Configuration is applicable with 19 
"non-time-managed-delay-enabled" (Boolean) parameter of low-level-rx-endpoint related by "name" to static-low-level-rx-20 
endpoint exposing endpoints ability to support non -time managed traffic. Default value of this parameter is FALSE, meaning 21 
endpoint supports time managed traffic by default. For details see: Note 2. 22 
5) NETCONF Client determines accessible static_low-level-rx-endpoint elements and static_low-level-tx-endpoint elements, 23 
including optional interface restrictions, that are suitable for the desired cell configuration (i.e. are linked with specific antenna 24 
arrays and are able to support desired type of traffic). 25 
6) NETCONF Client performs C/U -Plane transport configuration between O -DU and O -RU. NETCONF Client configures 26 
interfaces and creates processing-elements related to the interfaces offering access to desired endpoints (suitable in terms of 27 
capabilities and able to process signals related with desired [tr]x -array). Details of configuring interfaces and processing-28 
elements are described in Chapter 4.  29 
7) Once transport layer is configured, O-DU may perform initial verification of C/U Plane Transport Connectivity as described 30

12.3.2 Activation, deactivation and sleep 10 
The NETCONF Client performs activation by setting the value of the parameter “active” at tx-array-carrier element / rx-array-11 
carrier element to “ACTIVE”. 12 
The NETCONF Client performs deactivation by setting the value of the parameter “active” at tx -array-carrier element / rx -13 
array-carrier element to “INACTIVE” 14 
Communication between related U-Plane endpoints is enabled under condition, that for corresponding tx -array-carrier or rx -15 
array-carrier value of parameter “active” is “ACTIVE” and value of parameter “state” is “READY”. Otherwise communication 16 
is disabled. 17 
The NETCONF Client can put the tx-array-carrier / rx-array-carrier to sleep by setting value of parameter “active” in the 18 
corresponding tx-array-carrier element / rx-array-carrier element to “SLEEP”. 19 
A particular tx-array-carrier / rx-array-carrier is in sleep mode when value of its parameter “active” is “SLEEP” and value of 20 
its parameter “state” is “READY”. 21 
For detailed description of tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers please refer to description substatement in YANG models. 22 
Below diagram shows possible transitions and values combination to be followed by "active" and "state".  Combination or 23 
transitions outside of below diagram is not allowed. 24

12.4 Beamforming Configuration 2 
The beamforming functionality allows the O-RU to influence the angle of the main lobe of the signal which is radiated 3 
from/received by the O-RU. Beamforming support is optional and an O-RU shall indicate that it supports such 4 
functionality by indicating that it supports the “urn:o-ran:beamforming:x.y” namespace. 5 
A multi-band capable O-RU shall be able to support independent beamforming configuration on each of its supported tx-6 
arrays and/or rx-arrays depends on O-RU antenna configuration. 7 
12.4.1 Pre-Defined Beamforming Configuration 8 
In case the O-RU supports beamforming, the o-ran-beamforming.yang and o-ran-uplane-conf,yang modules are used to 9 
report the pre-defined relationship between supported beams to a NETCONF client. A band-number and/or capabilities-10 
group is used to uniquely identify separate tx-arrays and/or rx-arrays supported by a n O-RU with the beamforming 11 
configuration referencing the set of tx-arrays and rx-arrays that are associated with this band and/or capabilities-group. 12 
A default service area of  the O-RU is determined as the grid of pre -defined beams. When O -RU updates beamforming 13 
configuration as described in 12.4.2, the grid of pre-defined beams can be newly defined. In this case, the default service 14 
area is changed accordingly.  15 
O-RU may support new service area by applying tilt -offset to the given default service area in elevation and/or azimuth 16 
domains as described in 12.4.3. 17 
12.4.2 Beamforming Configuration Update 18 
This section provides the method to modify and to apply the beamforming configuration (weights, attributes and/or beam 19 
properties). The modification of the beamforming information is allowed only if O-RU supports the feature “MODIFY-20 
BF-CONFIG” used for defining the modification of beamforming configuration. 21 
The beamforming configuration is stored in the O-RU and comes from the O-RU’s software, treated in  Chapter 5. The 22 
O-RU shall locate the beamforming configuration file in the generic folder, i.e., O-RAN/beamforming/.  23 
To modify the beamforming configuration, the following steps are applied. 24 
1. NETCONF client can retrieve the file list of the O-RU’s folder: O-RAN/beamforming/. 25 
2. NETCONF client can trigger the upload of the beamforming configuration file from the O-RU’s folder. 26 
3. Operator can recover the uploaded file and edit the beamforming configuration file offline. 27 
4. NETCONF client can download the file to the original folder. 28 
The modified beamforming configuration file shall not have the same name as any other file in the folder. Its file name is 29 
the matter of implementation.  30 
The beam properties in o-ran-beamforming YAN G module contain coarse-fine, coarse-fine-beam-relation and 31 
neighbor-beam for each beam-id. This information is received from the O-RU as O-RU's capability at O-RU start-up 32 
and typically are used by the scheduler in O-DU. A NETCONF client (O-RU Controller) can modify t he beamforming 33 
information via file described in this section. When the beamforming configuration (weight, attribute and beam properties) 34 
is modified via file, the configuration of the beam properties list in the o-ran-beamforming YANG module should be 35 
modified together via the same file if affected by the modified weight and/or attribute.  36 
An O-RU supporting the modification of beamforming configuration shall support the storage of at least two beamforming 37 
files per simultaneous band-number and/or capabilities-group supported. For each band within a multi-band O-RU or 38 
each capabilities-group, one file corresponds to the pre-defined (factory, read-only) beamforming configuration and at 39 
least one file corresponds to a modified (read-write) beamforming file. The O-RU has the responsibility to remove existing 40 
file and prepares space for new file when the NETCONF client file-download rpc is issued. When the O-RU only supports 41 
the storage of a single modified  (read-write) beamforming file  per band of operation , i.e., number-of-writable-42 
beamforming-files = 1 the file-download operation for the modified beamforming configuration needs to be done while 43 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        112 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
neither tx-array-carriers nor rx-array-carriers are configured in the O-RU to avoid the removal of the modified 1 
beamforming configuration file for the current active software.  2 
If the O-RU supports the capability to store two or more modified beamforming configuration files per band of operation 3 
in the O-RU, i.e., number-of-writable-beamforming-files > 1,  the NETCONF file-download operation can be 4 
performed without any timing limitation. That's because the modified beamforming configuration file for the current 5 
beamforming configuration can be kept during the file-download operation. To apply the new modified beamforming 6 
configuration, the following steps are applied: 7 
1. The NETCONF client can download the file to the beamforming folder if the O-RU supports the capability number-8 
of-writable-beamforming-files > 1. 9 
2. The NETCONF client shall deactivate tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U -Plane configuration by 10 
setting "INACTIVE" for the active parameters, if they are ACTIVE. 11 
3. Optionally, the NETCONF client shall delete tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers, if O-RU doesn't support the 12 
capability update-bf-non-delete. 13 
4. Alternatively, the NETCONF client can trigger the download of the modified beamforming configuration file to the 14 
folder if the O-RU's capability is number-of-writable-beamforming-files =1. 15 
5. The NETCONF client shall activate the modified beamforming configuration by using: 16 
• activate-beamforming-config rpc and selecting the modified beamforming configuration file and the band-17 
number for which this modified configuration applies, 18 
• activate-beamforming-config-by-capability-group rpc and selecting the modified beamforming 19 
configuration file and the capabilities-group for which this modified configuration applies. 20 
6. If a NETCONF client subscribes to the notification beamforming-information-update and/or capability-group-21 
beamforming-information-update in advance, the O-RU sends such notification to the notification subscriber. 22 
Then the NETCONF client can subsequently retrieve beam properties in o-ran-beamforming YANG module via 23 
NETCONF <get> operation. 24 
7. Optionally, the NETCONF client shall create tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers again, if the O-RU doesn't 25 
support the capability update-bf-non-delete. 26 
8. The NETCONF Client shall activate tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U -Plane configuration by 27 
setting “ACTIVE” for active parameters. 28 
Then the new edited beamforming information is applied to the new tx-array-carriers and rx-array-carriers in the U-29 
Plane configuration. 30 
[Abnormal handling] If the O-RU fails to activate the edited beamforming configuration file correctly, i.e., rpc error for 31 
rpc activate-beamforming-config or activate-beamforming-config-by-capability-group, the O-RU shall revert back 32 
to the pre-defined/factory beamforming configuration file and report this to the NETCONF client. 33 
At the reset rpc, the beamforming configuration information is switched to the pre-defined beamforming configuration. 34 
Even though the reset operation is issued, the O-RU may store the modified beamforming configuration file in the folder, 35 
which is not used, if O-RU supports the capability persistent-bf-files to store them in the reset-persistent memory. 36 
The file format of the beamforming configuration is O-RU implementation specific. 37 
The diagrams below show two methods to modify the file of beamforming configuration information plus the method 38 
how to apply the modified file for beamforming configuration conformation to use. 39

12.4.3 Tilting Pre-defined Beams 2 
This section describes the optional capability by which the O-RU’s pre-defined beams may be tilted by using the 3 
“BEAM-TILT” feature defined in the o-ran-beamforming YANG model. This capability is an O-RU specific 4 
functionality, enabling adaptation of the service area associated with an O-RU without the need for operation of 5 
additional ALDs described in Chapter 11, or modifying the beamforming configuration using the “MODIFY-BF-6 
CONFIG” feature described in sub-section 12.4.2. 7 
 8 
Note, the operation of the feature “BEAM-TILT” is independent to the operation of the “MODIFY-BF-9 
CONFIG”. When the “MODIFY-BF-CONFIG” feature is used to define a new default service area, the 10 
“BEAM-TILT” feature may be used to apply tilt-offsets to the newly defined service area.  11 
 12 
O-RU can change the service are a by applying a tilt -offset to the elevation and/or azimuth pointing angles for the pre -13 
defined beams . This feature allows to shift beam characteristic of all predefined -beams in elevation and/or azimuth 14 
direction (i.e. changing the service area or sector coverage) while preserving the beam adjacency among the beams within 15 
grid of beams.  16 
Note, offset-elevation-tilt-angle values smaller than 0 represents an up -shift of the default service area towards 17 
the zenith (i.e., corresponding to a decrease in zenith angle) and values larger than 0 represent a down-shift of the 18 
default service area away from the zenith (i.e., corresponding to an increase in zenith angle). 19 
To shift service area of the O-RU in a different direction, O-RU controller shall check whether the O-RU supports feature 20 
BEAM-TILT feature during capabilities negotiation of the NETCONF session. In the case that O -RU supports the 21 
BEAM-TILT feature, at least one of the elevation-tilt-granularity and azimuth-tilt-granularity will be read as greater 22 
than zero value from O -RU. Tilting is a per band operation and hence the parameters are defined per band.  If O-RU 23 
supports BEAM-TILT feature, O-RU controller can configure the values of offset-elevation-tilt-angle and/or offset-24 
azimuth-tilt-angle the configuration values should meet the ranges and granularity information retrieved from 25 
predefined-beam-tilt-offset-information. 26 
 27 
Figure 55: Sequence diagram for predefined-beam-tilt-offset-information 28 
Depending on O-RU’s implementation, the O-RU may need some time to complete the change of service area according 29 
to the updated offset-elevation-tilt-angle and/or offset-azimuth-tilt-angle for a particular band-number. The O -RU 30 
shall report its capability via the parameter, run-time-tilt-offset-supported. For O -RU with run-time-tilt-offset-31 
supported = FALSE, changing the values in offset-elevation-tilt-angle and/or offset-azimuth-tilt-angle for a specific 32 


  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        116 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
band shall be allowed only if all tx-array-carriers/rx-array-carriers corresponding to the band is INACTIVE. When the 1 
service area change is completed in O-RU, the O-RU delivers the notification predefined-beam-tilt-offset-complete to 2 
inform the O-RU Controller which then may request to activate tx-array-carriers/rx-array-carriers in O-RU. For O-3 
RU with run-time-tilt-offset-supported = TRUE, neither changing the state of tx-array-carriers/rx-array-carriers nor 4 
delivering notification predefined-beam-tilt-offset-complete is required. 5

12.4.4 Dynamic Beamforming Control option 1 
As option, O-RU may support dynamic beamforming control mode. Support for this type of beamforming control can 2 
be recognized—in the case of weights-based dynamic beamforming—from value of parameter rt-bf-weights-update-3 
support (TRUE), and—in the case of attributes-based dynamic beamforming—from the value of parameter rt-bf-4 
attributes-update-support (TRUE), in o-ran-beamforming.yang module 5 
In dynamic beamforming control mode DU updates content of lookup table in O-RU using eCPRI C-Plane messages. 6 
For details of eCPRI messaging please see ORAN-WG4.CUS specification, chapter 5.4.2 "Scheduling and 7 
Beamforming Commands". 8 
Dynamically updated content of lookup table is further addressed by DU in the same way as it is done for static 9 
beamforming - by requesting particular Beam ID to be applied. 10 
In case dynamic beamforming control is supported, O-RU indicates following supplementary information using parent 11 
leaf "static-properties" in o-ran-beamforming.yang module. 12 
- beamforming type (frequency domain, time domain, hybrid) 13 
- beamforming weight compression format (optional) 14 
- available range of Beam IDs, that can be dynamically updated by DU. 15 
- supported time and frequency granularity for time domain and hybrid beamforming control. 16 
Note: Neighborhood relations between beams produced by beam IDs controlled by DU are unknown to O-RU, hence 17 
are not exposed. 18 
In the case of weights-based dynamic beamforming, to properly calculate beamforming weights DU needs to know 19 
antenna array geometry. This information DU obtains by reading the content of o-ran-uplane-conf.yang (list of tx-arrays 20 
and rx-arrays with their child parameters). Details of beamforming weight calculations are not a subject for M-Plane 21 
activity and as such are intentionally not covered in this specification. 22 
 23 
12.5 Antenna Calibration  24 
Some antennas need to be calibrated to ensure their intended performance. Antenna calibration operation is an option al 25 
capability whose operation is dependent on O-RU design, i.e. different O-RUs may support different types of calibration 26 
– periodic vs on-demand, different calibration duration – short/medium/long, etc. In this section, a common framework 27 
is defined which can accommodate various types of antenna calibration implementations.  28 
In this framework, the NETCONF client (O -DU) retrieves resource requirements for antenna calibration operation, e.g., 29 
timing and number of iterations/steps, from O -RU by getting the antenna-calibration-capabilities container defined in 30 
the o-ran-antenna-calibration YANG model. The O-DU can subscribe to antenna-calibration-required notifications to 31 
receive indications from the O-RU that calibration is required. When the O-RU indicates antenna calibration is required, 32 
or when the NETCONF Client decides to calibrate the O-RU, the NETCONF Client allocates time resources for antenna 33 
calibration and configures them in the O -RU using the start-antenna-calibration RPC request. The NETCONF clien t 34 
shall allocate the time resources for the calibration operation ensuring that these meet the minimum time necessary as 35 
reported by the O-RU using the antenna-calibration-capabilities. When available, the NETCONF client (O -DU) shall 36 
ensure that the freque ncy resources indicate d in the dl-calibration-frequency-chunk and ul-calibration-frequency-37 
chunk lists in the antenna-calibration-required notification are reserved for calibration operation, otherwise the 38 
NETCONF client shall consider that the full bandwidth of the carrier is being reserved for calibration operation.  39 
The O-RU shall perform antenna calibration operation using the time resources allocated in  the antenna-calibration-40 
start RPC and frequency resources declared in antenna-calibration-needed notification and shall notify the completion 41 
of the antenna calibration operation to the notification subscriber. The O-DU should be configured to not schedule user 42 
data using the time frequency resources identified for antenna calibration operation. The O-DU may schedule data during 43 
calibration operation using time frequency resources not identified for calibration operation. When the O -DU is 44 
scheduling user d ata during calibration process using resources not used for calibration, it shall only schedule DL user 45 
data in DL calibration symbols and UL user data in UL calibration symbols. 46 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        119 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
12.5.1 Overall Operation 1 
12.5.1.1 General 2 
During the O-RU “start-up” procedure, the NETCONF client (O-DU) retrieves the O-RU’s antenna calibration capability 3 
information including antenna calibration capability related parameters defined in o-ran-antenna-calibration.yang model. 4 
These parameters describe the O -RU’s time resource req uirements for calibration and the O -RU’s capability of 5 
performing “self-calibration”. The O -RU time resource requirements are described using the parameters number-of-6 
calibration-symbols-per-block-dl and number-of-calibration-symbols-per-block-ul. One symbol block corresponds 7 
to a set of consecutive symbols in time required for the calibration operation, and it is the basic time unit of calibration. 8 
Sets of symbol blocks are grouped into one calibration st ep and the O -RU shall indicate how many symbol blocks 9 
constitute one calibration step using the number-of-calibration-blocks-per-step-dl and number-of-calibration-blocks-10 
per-step-ul parameters. The O-RU indicates these parameters separately for downlink and uplink calibration. The O-RU 11 
shall also indicate the minimum time gap required between consecutive symbol block allocations ( interval-between-12 
calibration-block), number of calibration steps needed ( number-of-calibration-steps) and the minimum required time 13 
gap between consecutive calibration step allocations ( interval-between-calibration-step). Based on these parameters, 14 
the O-DU shall be able to allocate the time resources required for antenna calibration operation meeting the necessary 15 
time resources in dicated by the O -RU. If the O -RU supports mixed numerology, the highest possible numerology 16 
supported by the O -RU shall be used as the common reference per component carrier according to the CUS plane 17 
definition for slot indexing with mixed numerologies.  18 
12.5.1.2 Initiation 19 
Either the O-RU or O-DU may initiate calibration operation. The trigger condition for the O-DU and/or O-RU to initiate 20 
calibration is out of scope of this specification. The NETCONF client is assumed to have subscribed to the notificati ons 21 
defined in the o-ran-antenna-calibration YANG model.  When an O -RU determines that it needs to perform antenna 22 
calibration operation, it notifies the notification subscriber using the notification antenna-calibration-required, 23 
including a list of frequency ranges corresponding to the minimum frequency resources required for calibration, or, when 24 
the O -RU supports  the optional O -RU-COORDINATED-ANT-CAL feature, by using the antenna-calibration-25 
coordination notification. 26 
Upon reception of the antenna-calibration-required notification, the O-DU can allocate time frequency resources for 27 
calibration and can send the start-antenna-calibration RPC request, including the time resource allocation information 28 
for the antenna calibration. This operation is referred as ‘O-RU initiated antenna calibration’ operation.  29 
When coordinated-calibration-support is set to true, this indicates that the O-RU is able to determine a priori the time-30 
frequency resources required for antenna self -calibration and the O -RU uses antenna-calibration-coordination 31 
notification to indicate these to the O-DU instead of antenna-notification-required notification. When the coordinated-32 
calibration is supported and permitted, i.e., coordinated-calibration-support is true and coordinated-calibration-33 
allowed is true, the O-RU may perform a coordinated self-calibration procedure. An O-RU may also report the optional 34 
capability of configured-preparation-timer-supported which indicates that it supports configuration o f the preparedness 35 
timer that controls how far in advance of the coordinated self -calibration procedure the O -RU is required to send the 36 
notification of impacted resources. If configured by the NETCONF Client, the O-RU shall send the antenna-calibration-37 
coordination notification at least coordinated-ant-calib-prep-timer seconds before the operation of the coordinated antenna 38 
calibration procedure.  If such an optional capability is not supported , the O -RU shall indicate that time -frequency 39 
resources will be sent to a subscribed O-DU at least 60 seconds before the operation of the coordinated antenna calibration 40 
procedure. SFN wrap around will occur multiple times during these 60 seconds, this is handled according to statements 41 
in section 12.5.1.4. 42 
The O-DU shall not send a start-antenna-calibration RPC request when a coordinated antenna calibration period is in 43 
progress. The O-RU is allowed to reject such a request if it is received during a coordinated antenna calibration period.  44 
An O-DU receiving an antenna-calibration-coordination notification can beneficially use the indicated time-frequency 45 
resources to adapt its operation during the antenna calibration operation, e.g., consider the time -frequency resources as 46 
reserved for calibration. If no UL and/or DL frequency-chunk lists are provided in the notification, the O-DU may consider 47 
the full bandwidth of all configured UL and/or DL carriers reserved for calibration operation. If such U -Plane resources 48 
are scheduled by the O -DU, t he operation of the O -RU may be degraded, including performance of the calibration 49 
procedure and handling of DL and UL U-plane traffic and any associated performance counters. 50 
The O-DU may also autonomously initiate calibration operation, using the same start-antenna-calibration RPC request, 51 
i.e., without receiving the antenna-calibration-required notification message from O-RU. This operation is referred as 52 
‘O-DU initiated antenna calibration’ operation. If the O-RU has indicated the need for the calibration through sending the 53 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        120 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
antenna-calibration-required notification”, the O-DU shall consider that the use of frequency resources indicated using 1 
frequency range list within the notification as being affected during the calibration operation and if no frequency list is 2 
available, consider the full bandwidth of all configured carriers reserved is affected during calibration.  3 
After receiving “start-antenna-calibration RPC request” (antenna calibration start command), the O -RU shall send an 4 
RPC reply (antenna calibration start response) including ACCEPTED status to the NETCONF client, if the O-RU is able 5 
to start the calibration operation according to the time resources allocation information in the RPC request. Otherwise the 6 
O-RU shall include a REJECTED status in the RPC reply, with a suitable error reason such as “resource mask mismatch 7 
with O -RU antenna calibration capability”, “overlapped DL and UL masks”, “insufficient memory”, “O -RU internal 8 
reason” (if no other error reason matches the error condition) etc . If the O -RU does not receive a start-antenna-9 
calibration RPC request within 60 seconds after triggering the sending of the first antenna-calibration-required 10 
notification, the O-RU shall raise a major alarm “Triggering failure of antenna calibration”  (see Annex A for fault details). 11 
After the alarm is raised, the O -RU may resend the antenna-calibration-required notification multiple times. The O -12 
RU shall not re-send the antenna-calibration-required notification in periods shorter than 60 seconds.  13 
12.5.1.3 Self-Calibration Operation 14 
When the alarm “triggering failure of antenna calibration” alarm remains uncancelled, if self-calibration is supported and 15 
permitted, i.e., self-calibration-support is true and self-calibration-allowed is true, the O -RU may perform a self -16 
calibration procedure. The O -RU shall wait a minimum 60 seconds after raising a major alarm and receiving no start-17 
antenna-calibration RPC request from the NETCONF client before initiating its self -calibrate procedure. When self-18 
calibration is not supported or not permitted, i.e., self-calibration-support is false or self-calibration-allowed is false, 19 
the O-RU may upgrade the severity of the alarm to critical according to the sub-section 8.3.  20 
During the self-calibration, i.e., when the O -RU self-calibration-support set to true, requires no coordination of time -21 
frequency resources by the O-DU, i.e., the O-DU is permitted to continue to schedule user data during calibration process 22 
using the resources identified in antenn a-notification-required notification without impacting the operation of the 23 
calibration procedure.  24 
12.5.1.4 Calibration Completion 25 
The O-RU shall indicate completion of all types of  calibration procedures (i.e., rpc triggered, self -calibration and co -26 
ordinated self -calibration) using the antenna-calibration-result notification ( Calibration results) to the notification 27 
subscriber. If a self-calibration or co-ordinated self-calibration procedure completes but with status set to FAILURE, the 28 
O-RU may upgrade the severity of the alarm to critical. 29 
In some situations, SFN wrap around may happen causing O-DU and O-RU to interpret the ‘start-SFN’ parameter to point 30 
to different GPS seconds elapsed since GPS epoch. To avoid this situation, the O-DU to may decide not to schedule any 31 
user-plane data on the calibration time -frequency resources in all SFN cycles until the O -DU receives a n antenna-32 
calibration-result notification message from the O-RU. Once the calibration is complete, the O-DU schedules user data 33 
and sends C/U-Plane message as in normal operation state. 34
