12.5.2 O-RU Antenna Calibration Capability Parameter Configuration 1 
The antenna calibration framework is a generic framework designed to support various vendor specific implementations 2 
of O-RU calibration. Therefore, the framework does not describe the details of how the O-RU calibrates its antenna, rather 3 
it defines a generic framework with necessary message flows and parameters for ensuring that the time and frequency 4 
resources required for calibration are coordinated between the O -DU and O-RU. The following parameters describe the 5 
O-RU’s time resource needed for calibration. 6 
- self-calibration-support: boolean value indicates whether O-RU is capable of supporting self-calibration.  7 
- number-of-calibration-symbols-per-block-dl: indicates how many consecutive symbols are required for DL antenna 8 
calibration operation, i.e. the size of DL Symbol-block. 9 
- number-of-calibration-symbols-per-block-ul: indicates how many consecutive symbols are required for UL antenna 10 
calibration operation, i.e. the size of UL Symbol-block. 11 
- interval-between-calibration-blocks: if a time interval is required between consecutive antenna calibration operation, 12 
this indicates the required time value as unit of symbols. A common value is used here for the intervals between DL -DL 13 
blocks, UL-UL blocks, DL-UL blocks and UL-DL blocks, which is the largest minimum interval required between any 14 
two adjacent calibration blocks. It shall be any value that O-RU implementation requires within this parameter range. 15 
- number-of-calibration-blocks-per-step-dl: indicates how many blocks are required for one step of DL antenna 16 
calibration operation. 17 
- number-of-calibration-blocks-per-step-ul: indicates how many blocks are required for one step of UL antenna 18 
calibration operation. 19 
- interval-between-calibration-steps: if a time interval is required between consecutive steps of antenna calibration 20 
operation, define indicates the required time value as unit of radio frames. It can be any value that the O -RU 21 
implementation requires within the defined parameter range. 22 
- number-of-calibration-steps: shows how many steps is required for whole DL/UL antenna calibration operation. 23 
The following figure shows the relationship between the various antenna calibration capabilities parameters described 24 
above. 25

12.5.3 antenna-calibration-required Notification Parameters 29 
If the O-RU initiates the calibration operation, the O-RU notifies the notification subscriber (O-DU) using the antenna-30 
calibration-required notification message, including the O-RU’s frequency resource requirements. The O-RU is able 31 
to indicate non-contiguous frequency “chunks” necessary for calibration using the dl-calibration-frequency-chunk 32 
and ul-calibration-frequency-chunk lists. These lists use the parameters below to describe the frequency resources 33 
required for calibration: 34 
- start-calibration-frequency-dl: indicates the lowest frequency value in Hz of the frequency range is required for DL 35 
antenna calibration operation. 36 
- end-calibration-frequency-dl: indicates the highest frequency value in Hz of the frequency range is required for DL 37 
antenna calibration operation. 38 
- start-calibration-frequency-ul: indicates the lowest frequency value in Hz of the frequency range is required for UL 39 
antenna calibration operation. 40 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        123 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
- end-calibration-frequency-ul: indicates the highest frequency value in Hz of the frequency range is required for UL 1 
antenna calibration operation. 2 
12.5.4 Start-antenna-calibration RPC Request Parameters 3 
The NETCONF Client sends the “start-antenna-calibration RPC request” including the time resource allocation 4 
parameters. These parameters indicate the exact symbols, slots, and frames that can be used for calibration. 5 
Note, because the NETCONF Client (O-DU) is responsible for allocating the time resources for calibration with 6 
the knowledge of UL and DL configuration, dynamic TDD operation is implicitly supported.  7 
The resource allocation information about symbol, slot, and frame are indicated using bitmasks for downlink and uplink 8 
calibration separately. The start SFN of the first calibration step is sent to the O-RU to synchronize the calibration 9 
starting point at both O-DU and O-RU. When indicated, the O-RU shall use the frequency resources indicated using the 10 
frequency ranges in the “NETCONF antenna-calibration-required notification” message for calibration.   11 
Following table lists the parameters configured in the O-RU using the “start-antenna-calibration RPC request” 12 
Parameters Type / Range Descriptions 
symbol-bitmask-dl string Bitmask indicating DL calibration symbol within a calibration slot. First 
character in the string indicate first symbol, next character in the string 
indicate second symbol and so on. Value 1 indicates that the symbol is 
allocated for calibration and 0 means the symbol shall not be used for 
calibration. 
Symbol-bitmask-ul string Bitmask indicating UL calibration symbol within a calibration slot. First 
character in the string indicate first symbol, next character in the string 
indicate second symbol and so on. Value 1 indicates that the symbol is 
allocated for calibration and 0 means the symbol shall not be used for 
calibration. 
Slot-bitmask-dl string  Bitmask indicating DL calibration slot within a calibration frame. First 
character in the string indicate first slot, next character in the string indicate 
second slot and so on. Value 1 indicates that the slot is allocated for 
calibration and 0 means the slot shall not be used for calibration. 
Slot-bitmask-ul string  Bitmask indicating UL calibration slot within a calibration frame. First 
character in the string indicate first slot, next character in the string indicate 
second slot and so on. Value 1 indicates that the slot is allocated for 
calibration and 0 means the slot shall not be used for calibration. 
Frame-bitmask-dl string  Bitmask indicating DL calibration frame within a calibration step. First 
character in the string indicate first radio frame equal to the start-SFN, next 
character in the string indicate the next frame and so on. Value 1 indicates 
that the frame is allocated for calibration and 0 means the frame shall not 
be used for calibration. 
Frame-bitmask-ul string  Bitmask indicating UL calibration frame within a calibration step. First 
character in the string indicate first radio frame equal to the start-SFN, next 
character in the string indicate the next frame and so on. Value 1 indicates 
that the frame is allocated for ca libration and 0 means the frame shall not 
be used for calibration.

12.5.5 Example Antenna Calibration Operation  14 
This subsection illustrates an example of antenna calibration operation. For simplicity,  the O-RU is the initiator in this 15 
example, but either O-RU or O-DU could initiate antenna calibration operation. In this example, the TDD configuration 16 
is assumed as shown in the following figure. 17

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Figure 59: Example of TDD configuration 2 
 3 
This example illustrates calibration operation where an O -RU requires DL and UL antenna calibration operation in o-4 
ran-antenna-calibration.yang with 2 calibration steps; within each step, 64 DL calibration blocks with 4 continuous DL 5 
symbols in each calibration block and 32 UL calibration blocks with 1 continuous UL symbol in each calibration block 6 
are required. Between each calibration block, a length of minimum 3 symbols interval is required, and a length of 7 
minimum 5 frames interval is required between consecutive calibration steps.  8 
Once antenna calibration operation is required by the O-RU, an antenna-calibration-required notification is sent to the 9 
notification subscriber (O-DU), including the O -RU’s frequency resources requirement in a list of frequency ranges in 10 
Hz, which in this example uses a single chunk of frequencies from 1.8GHz  to 1.82GHz. The O-DU considers that the 11 
frequency range indicate d in the antenna-calibration-required notification will be subsequently used during antenna 12 
calibration. The O-DU will allocate time resources for antenna calibration based on the TDD configuration together with 13 
the O-RU DL and UL antenna calibration capab ility, then configure the antenna calibration using the start-antenna-14 
calibration RPC request. In this example, 64 DL calibration blocks in each calibration step are allocated in 4 frames, 15 
within each frame, 8 DL slots are allocated and within each DL slot, 2 calibration blocks are allocated for DL calibration. 16 
In parallel, 32 UL calibration blocks in each calibration step are allocated in 4 frames, within each frame, 4 UL slots are 17 
allocated and within each UL slot, 2 calibration blocks are allocated for UL calibration. To guarantee the interval between 18 
2 calibration steps, the size of each calibration step is set to 10 frames. At least 3 symbols interval between each calibration 19 
block is also guaranteed in symbol bitmasks.  The O-DU may allocate larger inte rvals than O-RU requires as shown in 20 
this example where a 9 symbols interval is allocated instead of the minimum of 3 symbols after second UL symbol block 21 
in all UL calibration slots. 22

12.5.6 Calibration with multiple timing resource sets 3 
 4 
The O-RU may indicate its ability to support  multiple time resource configuration sets for antenna calibration by 5 
support of the feature  O-RU-COORDINATED-ANT-CAL-MULTIPLE-TIME-RESOURCE in o-ran-antenna-6 
calibration.yang module. The feature is intended to extend the antenna calibration framework to support multiple time 7 
resources instead of single time resource supported. This capability can be used by the O-RU to specify unique 8 
calibration time resources for different calibration types. O-RU which supports this capability, exposes a list of time 9 
resources (antenna-calibration-multiple-time-resource-list). O-RU indicates desired set of time resources in ‘antenna-10 
calibration-multiple-time-resource’ notification using specific value of ‘antenna-calibration-time-resource-index’ 11 
parameter. 12 
This feature applies to O-RU initiated calibration where O-RU supporting this feature can use new notification 13 
‘antenna-calibration-multiple-time-resource’ containing the parameter ‘antenna-calibration-time-resource-index’, 14 
defined in Sec 12.5.7. Based on the index value in the notification respective antenna calibration time resource values 15 
should apply while initiating “start-antenna-calibration RPC request”. O-RU can use this calibration feature only in 16 
case O-DU configured parameter ‘coordinated-calibration-multiple-time-resources-allowed’ is set to TRUE. 17 
Note: At any point in time only one calibration timing resources should be indicated the O-RU. 18

resource-params notification message. Remaining parameter list of this notification includes the frequency resources 23 
required for calibration same as ‘antenna-calibration-required’ described in Section 12.5.2: 24

12.6 Static configuration for PRACH and SRS 1 
PRACH and raw SRS are periodic. Their location in time and frequency resources is constant for all periods. This makes 2 
it feasible to configure PRACH and raw SRS with M-Plane in a sense that handling PRACH and / or raw SRS processing 3 
by assigned low-level-rx-endpoints does not require real-time control through C-Plane messages. 4 
Static configuration of PRACH and SRS with M-Plane needs to cover following aspects: 5 
- Configuration of frequency resources assigned to PRACH / SRS 6 
- Configuration of time resources assigned to PRACH / SRS (including PRACH / SRS periodicity) 7 
- Configuration of compression, iFFT and SCS 8 
- Assignment of HW resources (low-level-rx-endpoints) for processing of PRACH / SRS 9 
 10 
Static configurations shall be provided to the O-RU as part of carrier configuration - before the configured carrier is 11 
activated. Static PRACH / SRS configuration provided for already active carrier shall be rejected by the O-RU. 12 
 13 
Note: In case a static-low-level-rx-endpoint exposes parameter static-config-supported with value NONE – such 14 
endpoint does not offer support for static configuration of PRACH nor SRS reception. 15 
 16 
Note: In case the configuration provided to O-RU contains records for TDD pattern(s), PRACH patterns and/or 17 
SRS patterns, the O-RU validates consistency between patterns. Configuration where there is collision between 18 
patterns detected, shall be rejected by the O-RU. 19 
12.6.1 Static configuration for PRACH processing 20 
The O-RU exposes its ability to support static PRACH configuration by support of the feature PRACH-STATIC-21 
CONFIGURATION-SUPPORTED in o-ran-module-cap.yang module. Presence of this feature means, that at least one 22 
of static -low-level-rx-endpoints offered by the O -RU supports static configuration for PRACH. From the model 23 
perspective, static PRACH configuration is supported by static -low-level-rx-endpoints having the parameter static-24 
config-supported exposed as PRACH. Such static -low-level-rx-endpoint can be referenced by low -level-rx-endpoint 25 
designated for reception of PRACH. Specific PRACH configuration may be utilised by the low -level-rx-endpoint 26 
according to the optional parameter static-prach-configuration. 27 
Note: a single low-level-rx-endpoint can only reference to single instance of static-prach-configuration. However, 28 
a single static-prach-configuration may be referenced by many low-level-rx-endpoints. 29 
If parameters related to static PRACH configuration are set by NETCONF Client – real-time C-Plane control for PRACH 30 
opportunities shall not be provided to the O-RU, allowing for static configuration to be utilised. 31

12.6.1.3 Operation 13 
Static PRACH configuration shall be set and rx-endpoints shall be linked to it before rx-array-carrier activation. On 14 
carrier activation, the O-RU starts receiving RF signals corresponding to the configured prach-patterns list. 15 
Specifically, the O-RU receives RF signals corresponding to the prach-pattern p when  16 
mod( 𝑛𝑓, pattern-period ) = frame-numberp and  17 
𝑛𝑠𝑓 = sub-frame-idp and  18 
t = time-offsetp 19 
where 20 
𝑛𝑓 is the system frame number,   21 
mod( x, y ) is remainder of division of x by y, 22 
𝑛𝑠𝑓 is the subframe number within system frame 𝑛𝑓, 23 
t is the time since start of subframe 𝑛𝑠𝑓, 24 
frame-number, sub-frame-idp and time-offsetp are parameters of prach-pattern p, 25 
pattern-period is a parameter of PRACH configuration. 26 
Once the RF signal corresponding to the PRACH repetition 𝑛𝑟 in PRACH occasion 𝑛𝑜 is received and processed, the 27 
O-RU sends the corresponding IQ values in a U-plane message or messages with header fields set as follows: 28

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
frameId = mod( floor( 𝑛𝑓 / pattern-period ) • pattern-period + frame-numberp, 256 ) 1 
(note: this corresponds to 𝑛𝑓 value captured when prach-pattern p started) 2 
subframeId = sub-framep, 3 
slotId = zero-based PRACH occasion number within PRACH pattern, 4 
symbolId = zero-based PRACH repetition number within PRACH occasion, 5 
sectionId = 4095, 6 
startPrbu = floor( ( re-offsetp + guard-tone-low-re ) / 12 ), 7 
numPrbu = ceil( (re-offsetp + guard-tone-low-re + num-prach-re ) / 12 ) - startPrbu.  8 
where 9 
𝑛𝑓 is the system frame number,   10 
mod( x, y ) is remainder of division of x by y, 11 
floor( x ) is largest integer smaller than or equal to x, 12 
ceil( x ) is smallest integer greater than or equal to x, 13 
frame-numberp, sub-frame-numberp and re-offsetp are parameters of prach-pattern p.  14 
pattern-period, guard-tone-low-re and num-prach-re are parameters of PRACH configuration. 15 
If data section is subdivided due to application level fragmentation, resulting values of startPrbu and numPrbu shall be 16 
calculated as per general rules. If multiple PRACH repetitions are scheduled at the same time at different re-offset 17 
frequencies, the O-RU shall send corresponding data sections in one U-Plane message following message size 18 
restrictions.  19 
12.6.2 Static configuration for raw SRS processing 20 
The O-RU exposes its ability to support static raw SRS configuration by support of the feature SRS-STATIC-21 
CONFIGURATION-SUPPORTED in o-ran-module-cap.yang module. Presence of this feature means, that at least one 22 
of static-low-level-rx-endpoints offered by the O-RU supports static configuration for raw SRS reception. From the model 23 
perspective, static SRS  configuration is supported by static -low-level-rx-endpoints having the parameter static-config-24 
supported exposed as SRS. Such static-low-level-rx-endpoint can be referenced by a low -level-rx-endpoint designated 25 
for reception of SRS. Specific SRS configuration may be utilised by the low-level-rx-endpoint according to the optional 26 
parameter static-srs-configuration. 27 
Note: a single low-level-rx-endpoint can only reference to single instance of static -srs-configuration. However, a 28 
single static-srs-configuration may be referenced by many low-level-rx-endpoints. 29 
If parameters related to static SRS configuration are set by NETCONF Client – real-time C-Plane control for SRS shall 30 
not be provided to the O-RU, allowing for static configuration to be utilised. 31 
Static SRS configuration is used to configure NDM (Non-Delay Managed) raw SRS (Sounding Reference Signal) 32 
patterns in a static manner, such that raw SRS U-Plane traffic can be processed by the O-RU without receiving C-Plane 33 
messages conveying real-time raw SRS configuration. Raw SRS may capture non-beamformed (beam-id = 0) or 34 
beamformed (beam-id != 0) signals and uses non-delay managed U-Plane messages. 35 
One static-srs-configuration instance allows to configure a set of SRS patterns. For a single SRS configuration, all 36 
SRS patterns repeat over the period defined by pattern-period parameter for such SRS configuration. SRS patterns 37 
corresponding to a single SRS configuration shall not overlap in terms of time and frequency.  38 
An O-RU shall reject any configuration where the number of patterns in single static SRS configuration exceeds the 39 
number exposed by capability parameter max-srs-patterns in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module. 40 
12.6.2.1 Operation 41 
Static SRS configuration shall be set and rx-endpoints shall be linked to it before rx-array-carrier activation. On carrier 42 
activation, the O-RU starts receiving RF signals corresponding to the configured srs-patterns list. Specifically, the O-43 
RU receives RF signal and sends corresponding U-plane messages as if, for each configured srs-pattern p, each rx-44 
endpoint linked with the SRS configuration received C-plane messages with fields:  45 
dataDirection = 0 (RX), 46 
payloadVersion = 0,  47 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        131 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
filterIndex = 0, 1 
frameId = mod( 𝑛𝑓, 256 ), 2 
subframeId = sub-frame-idp, 3 
slotId = slot-idp, 4 
startSymbolId = start-symbol-idp, 5 
numberOfSections = 1, 6 
sectionId = 4095, 7 
rb = 0, 8 
symInc = 0, 9 
startPrbc = start-prbcp, 10 
numPrbc = num-prbcp, 11 
reMask = 0xFFF, 12 
numSymbol = num-symbolp, 13 
ef=0, 14 
beamId = beam-idp, 15 
where 16 
𝑛𝑓 is the system frame number,   17 
mod( x, y ) is remainder of division of x by y, 18 
sub-frame-idp slot-idp, start-symbol-idp, beam-idp, start-prbcp and num-prbcp are parameters of srs-pattern p, 19 
12.7 TDD pattern configuration 20 
The O-RU exposes its ability to support TDD pattern configuration by support of the feature CONFIGURABLE-TDD-21 
PATTERN-SUPPORTED in o-ran-module-cap.yang module. Presence of this feature means, that at least one of static-22 
low-level-[tr]x-endpoints offered by the O-RU supports configuration for TDD pattern , so that these static-low-level-23 
[tr]x-endpoints can be used (through low-level-[tr]x-endpoints) by [tr]x-array-carriers having configurable TDD pattern 24 
assigned.  25 
Note: Configured TDD pattern shall not be violated by C-Plane and U-Plane messages. 26 
Note: In case configuration provided to O-RU contains records for TDD pattern(s), PRACH patterns and/or SRS 27 
patterns, O-RU validates consistency between patterns. Configuration where there is collision between patterns 28 
detected, shall be rejected by O-RU. 29 
From the model perspective, configuration for TDD pattern is supported by static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoints having 30 
parameter configurable-tdd-pattern exposed as TRUE. Such static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoint can be respectively 31 
referenced by low -level-[tr]x-endpoint designated to serve for [tr]x-array-carrier having preconfigured TDD pattern 32 
assigned. Specific configuration of the TDD patter n may be utilised by [tr]x -array-carrier according to the optional 33 
parameter configurable-tdd-pattern.  34 
Absence of leaf configurable-tdd-pattern at [tr]x-array-carrier means, that such [tr]x-array-carrier has no configurable-35 
tdd-pattern assigned. 36 
A configurable TDD pattern can be assigned to a [tr]x -array-carrier under the condition, that all static -low-level-[tr]x-37 
endpoints serving such an [tr]x-array-carrier expose value of capability configurable-tdd-pattern-supported as TRUE. 38 
A s ingle [tr]x -array-carrier can only  reference to single instance of configurable -tdd-pattern. Whereas, a s ingle 39 
configurable-tdd-pattern shall be referenced by all cooperating [tr]x -array-carriers serving for a specific [tr]x-array. 40 
Linkage between tx -array-carriers and rx -array-carriers configured to use the same configurable -tdd-pattern must be 41 
assured by the entity responsible for configuration provisioning to O-RU. For example, ensuring that all cooperating [tr]x-42 
array-carriers use static -low-level-[tr]x-endpoints (through low -level-[tr]x-endpoints) having the same value of tdd-43 
group. The practical implication of this is that static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoints exposing the same value of parameter tdd-44 
group must be used by low -level-[tr]x-endpoints serving for [tr]x-array-carriers having the same TDD switching points 45 
and the same directions to the air interface granted by TDD patterns they are configured to use. 46 
Note: M-Plane model allows an O-RU to be configured with more than one TDD patterns. This is capability can 47 
be used by O-RUs having more than one [tr]x-array. 48 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        132 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
A single TDD pattern configuration consists of list of records. Each single record contains details for frame-offset and 1 
direction of signal that must be applied at the moment a specific frame-offset occurs at air interface. Supported 2 
directions are UL (uplink), DL (downlink) and GP (neither uplink nor downlink). 3 
Note: Assignment of configurable-tdd-pattern to a [tr]x-array-carrier is only possible in case all following 4 
conditionals are met: 5 
- O-RU supports feature CONFIGURABLE-TDD-PATTERN-SUPPORTED. 6 
- all static-low-level-[tr]x-endpoint configured to serve for a specific [tr]x-array-carrier have capability 7 
configurable-tdd-pattern set to TRUE 8 
12.8 C-Plane Message Limits 9 
The O -RU exposes i ts ability to support C -Plane message  limits by including support of the feature CPLANE-10 
MESSAGE-LIMITS in o-ran-wg4-features.yang module. Refer to Sec 5.6 .2 of CUS-Plane specification to understand 11 
details of this feature. The presence of this feature means, that in addition to an O-RU's "per-endpoint processing limits" 12 
e.g. endpoint -section-capacity, endpoint -beam-capacity, endpoint -prb-capacity, an O -RU may also have “per-cplane 13 
message limits”. To support this feature on a per endpoint basis, a new flag 'cplane-message-processing-limits-14 
required' is added to 'endpoint-types' to indicate an endpoint’s requirement to support C -Plane message processing 15 
limits. The flag shall be set to true for the endpoints to which C -Plane message processing limits apply. An additional 16 
configuration flag 'cplane-message-processing-limits-enabled' is added to low-level-[tr]x-endpoints (applicable only 17 
for endpoints to which C -Plane limit requirement is exposed by O -RU) to enable the O-DU to use this feature on a per 18 
endpoint basis. 19 
1. If the O -DU supports C -Plane message processing limits, it can choose to indicate it adheres to the limits by 20 
configuring schema node 'cplane-message-processing-limits-enabled= true'. In such case, the O-DU shall follow 21 
limits specified by the parameters ' max-beams-per-slot-cplane-limits-enabled'  and 'max -highest-priority-22 
sections-per-slot-cplane-limits-enabled'  when forming C-Plane messages. 23 
2. If O-DU does not support C -Plane message processing limits by configuring schema node 'cplane-message-24 
processing-limits-enabled= false' OR O -RU does not indicate it supports the CPLANE -MESSAGE-LIMITS 25 
YANG feature, no C -Plane message limits shall apply and O -RU continues to use endpoint capacity limits 26 
specified in existing endpoint by per -endpoint limits e.g. endpoint -section-capacity, endpoint-beam-capacity, 27 
endpoint-prb-capacity. 28 
 29 
Chapter 13 Licensed-Assisted Access 30 
13.1 Introduction: 31 
Licensed-assisted access (LAA) leverages the carrier -aggregation (CA) functionality. With LAA, CA is performed 32 
between licensed and unlicensed component carriers (CCs). This enables the LAA system to opportunistically benefit 33 
from using unlicensed spectrum (e.g., UNII bands in the 5 GHz spectrum) to enhance the aggregated capacity of the O -34 
RU with the objective of enhancing the downlink throughput. 35 
Several modifications in the RAN are needed to enable LAA in the O -DU and O-RU such as listen -before-talk (LBT), 36 
discontinuous transmission, carrier-selection, discovery reference signal (DRS) transmission, etc. This section is focused 37 
on the LAA-related messages and procedures needed in the M -plane. The C -plane related messages are defined in the 38 
CUS-plane spec [2]. 39 
This version of the M -plane spec supports only LAA based on Rel. 13 of the 3GPP specs, where transmission on the 40 
unlicensed spec trum can be done only in the downlink direction. The support of eLAA Rel. 14 (i.e., enabling UL 41 
transmission on the unlicensed spectrum) may be included in a later version of the M-plane spec.  42 
The modifications at M-plane to Support LAA can be summarized as follows: 43 
i) LAA-initiation process: O-DU learns about O-RU capabilities and configures it.  44 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        133 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
• O-RU LAA Support: The O -RU indicates it supports LAA by including support for the "urn:o -1 
ran:laa:x.y" and "urn:o -ran:laa-operations:x.y" namespaces in its ietf -yang-library model (RFC 7895) 2 
[20]. 3 
• O-RU LAA Capability Information: When the LAA feature is enabled, leafs corresponding to LAA -4 
related O-RU capabilities, such as the number of supported LAA SCarriers, maximum LAA buffer size, 5 
etc, are conveyed via the M-plane to the O-DU as part of the o-ran-module-cap.yang module.  6 
• O-RU LAA Configuration: The NETCONF client configures the unlicensed LAA component carrier 7 
with the LAA -related parameters such as the energy -detection threshold, DRS measurement timing 8 
configuration (DMTC) period, etc. as part of the o -ran-uplane-config.yang module. The configuration 9 
of the number of LAA SCarriers, multi-carrier type, etc. is performed using the o-ran-laa.yang Module. 10 
• For explanation of the LAA -initiation process, please refer to Figure 4 in Chapter 3, where the O -RU 11 
LAA capability info is conveyed within the “Retrieval of O-RU information” step, while the O-RU LAA 12 
configurations are conveyed in “Configuring the O-RU operational parameters” step in Figure 4.  13 
ii) Carrier-selection: Selecting the best channel in the unlicensed band, both initially and dynamically over time.  14 
 15 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        134 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00

13.2 LAA-initiation Process   3 
13.2.1 LAA Module Capabilities 4 
During LAA-initiation, the O-RU reports its LAA capabilities to the NETCONF client. These capabilities are sent at the 5 
start up as part of the o-ran-module-cap.yang module. The attributes included are: 6 
(1) sub-band-frequency-ranges: The unlicensed sub -bands (e.g., 46A, 46B, etc.) that are supported at the O -RU and 7 
their frequency ranges 8 
(2) number-of-laa-scarriers (uint8): Number of LAA SCarriers that the O-RU can support.  9 


  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        135 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
(3) maximum-laa-buffer-size (uint16): Maximum O-RU buffer size in Kilobytes (KB) per CC. This parameter is needed 1 
at the O-DU to know how much data can be sent in advance and stored at the O-RU to address the LBT uncertainty.  2 
(4) maximum-processing-time (uint16): Maximum O-RU Processing time in microseconds at the O -RU to handle the 3 
received/transmitted packets from/to the O -DU. This parameter is needed at the O -DU to determine the time where it 4 
needs to send the data to the O-RU.  5 
 (5) self-configure (Boolean): Capability to manage the contention window at the O-RU. Based on the CUS-spec, there 6 
are two modes of operation for LAA, 1) when the contention window is managed by the O-DU, and 2) when the 7 
contention window is managed by the O-RU. This field is set to True if the O-RU can manage the contention window 8 
locally.  9 
13.2.2 LAA O-RU Parameter Configuration 10 
The second stage of the LAA -initiation process is the configuration message (using RPC edit -config). In this message, 11 
the O -DU configures the O -RU with the required parameters in the downlink direction. LAA parameters can be 12 
configured by Netconf Client after capability exchange is finished. It can also be sent as needed, to reconfigure the O-RU 13 
with new parameters (e.g., ed-threshold-pdsch, etc.). The attributes of this message (o-ran-laa.yang Module) include: 14 
(1) number-of-laa-scarriers (uint8): Number of LAA SCarriers to be used at the O-RU. This number should be less 15 
than or equal the number reported by the O-RU in its module capabilities.  16 
(2) multi-carrier-type (Enumeration): This value indicates the list of multi carrier types (A1, A2, B1, B2) which as 17 
subsection 15.1.5 in [32].  18 
(3) multi-carrier-tx (Boolean): This value indicates whether self-deferral is activated or not. “True” indicates 19 
transmission on channel access win (i.e., no self-deferral). “False” indicates mutual transmission on multiple carriers. 20 
(4) multi-carrier-freeze (Boolean): This value indicates if the absence of other technology in the unlicensed band can 21 
be guaranteed. This attribute can only be used when the multi-carrier-type is A1. “False” indicates that absence of other 22 
technology is not guaranteed. 23 
(5) laa-ending-dwpts-supported (Boolean): This value indicates whether LAA ending in Downlink Pilot Time Slot 24 
(DwPTS) is supported. 25 
(6) laa-starting-in-second-slot-supported (Boolean): This value indicates LAA starting in second slot is supported. 26 
LAA carrier configurations (o-ran-uplane-conf.yang Module) include:  27 
(1) ed-threshold-pdsch (int8): This value indicates the energy detection (ED) threshold for LBT for PDSCH and for 28 
measurements in dBm. 29 
(2) ed-threshold-drs (int8): This value indicates the ED threshold for LBT for DRS in dBm. 30 
 (4) tx-antenna-ports (uint8): This value indicates the Tx antenna ports for DRS.  31 
(5) transmission-power-for-drs (int8): This value indicates the offset of CRS power to reference signal power (dB). 32 
(6) dmtc-period (enumeration): This value indicates DMTC period in milliseconds.  33 
(7) dmtc-offset (uint8): This value indicates DMTC offset in Subframes. 34 
(8) lbt-timer (uint16): This value indicates LBT Timer in milliseconds. 35 
If Self Configure capability is set to “true”, the following parameters are also needed to be configured. For every traffic 36 
priority class, the O -DU needs to configure maximum CW usage counter. This value indicates the maximum value of 37 
counter which shows how many max congestion window value is used for back off number of each priority class traffic. 38 
This value is defined at section 15.1.3 of [32] as K. Based on the 3GPP specification, this value is selected by O-RU from 39 
the set of values {1, 2, …, 8} 40 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        136 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
13.3 Carrier-Selection  1 
13.3.1 LAA Measurements 2 
The function of the message “ rpc start-measurements” is to order the O -RU to start measurements. This message can 3 
be used for carrier selection initially or dynamically over time. O -RU sends RPC response where status==ACCEPTED 4 
(positive case) or REJECTED (negative case). O -RU performs measurement and delivers result with respect to max 5 
response time. If result is not ready on time - O-RU sends notification with "measurement-success" == FALSE and with 6 
appropriate failure reason. For every configured band, the O-RU informs the NETCONF client whether the measurement 7 
was successful or not. For bands with successful measurements, the O-RU reports the occupancy ratio and average RSSI 8 
for each channel. For bands with failure measurements, the O -RU includes the reason (e.g., TIMEOUT when the O -RU 9 
is not able to finish the measurement for this specific band).  10 
The occupancy ratio of a given channel is defined as the percentage of the busy duration (i.e., measured signal power is 11 
larger than the energy -detection threshold) to the total measurement duration of this specific channel. The energy -12 
detection threshold is specified in the o -ran-uplan-conf.yang module using the ed-threshold-pdsch leaf. Note that this 13 
threshold is the same as the energy -detection threshold used for LBT for PDSCH transmission. The total measurement 14 
duration per channel is specif ied in o-ran-laa-operation module using the duration-per-channel leaf. The range of the 15 
occupancy ratio is from 0% (no signal is detected over the total measurement duration per channel) to 100% (i.e., channel 16 
was always occupied during measurement).  17 
The average RSSI of the measured channel is the measured power of this specific channel averaged over the total 18 
measurement duration per channel. This parameter is reported to the NETCONF client in dBm and takes a value from the 19 
range 0 dBm to -128 dBm. 20 
13.3.2 LAA Carrier Frequency Configuration 21 
After receiving the measurements, the NETCONF client configures the O -RU with the new channel(s), if needed. For 22 
every component carrier (CC) that needs to be configured with a new center frequency, the O -DU will need t o first 23 
deactivate the TX carrier, delete it, then create a new TX carrier (with the new center carrier frequency as well as any 24 
other new configurations), and then activate the TX carrier again to start OTA operation. The procedure for 25 
deactivating/deleting/creating/activating the carrier is explained in Section 12.3: Carrier Configuration, in the M -plane 26 
specification and elaborated in Figure 48. Note that the creation of LAA carriers is identical to the creation of regular 27 
carriers but in the unlicensed bands. O-RU responds to the configuration request with success or failure.  28 
Note also that carrier -selection algorithm at the O -DU (i.e., selecting the “best” channel ba sed on the reported 29 
measurements from the O-RU) is an implementation issue and is out of the scope of this document. 30

14.1 Architecture 1 
The NETCONF client (O-RU Controller) establishes M-Plane connection individually to each O-RU, where the O-RUs 2 
are operating in either cascade mode or FHM mode 3 
 4 
Figure 67: M-Plane and C/U-Plane Connectivity for Cascade and FHM Modes  5 
In this figure, solid lines indicate C/U-plane interface and dotted lines indicate M-plane interface. Therefore, from the M-6 
Plane point of view, the same architecture model can be applied as specified in Chapt er 2.1.2. New functionality which 7 
is required to be added, together with existing functionality which is required to be enhanced are specified in sub-sections 8 
14.2 to 14.5. There are no changes to the functionality described in the following chapters and t heir associated YANG 9 
models:   10 
- Chapter 5 : Software Management 11 
- Chapter 8 : Fault Management 12 
- Chapter 9 : File Management 13 
 14 
A NETCONF client with suitable privileges is able to trigger a reset procedure for each O-RU. It is strongly recommended 15 
that when triggering the reset procedures for multiple O -RUs, a NETCONF client should order the procedures such that 16 
a reset of an individual O -RU does not affect th e operation of other O -RUs operating in either cascade or FHM mode.  17 
This can be achieved by correct ordering of the triggering of the reset procedure between the different O-RUs. For example, 18 
when triggering a reset involving multiple O-RUs operating in cascade mode, the ordering of the reset trigger sent by the 19 
NETCONF client should be done beginning with the last (most -southern) O-RU to the first (most northern) O -RU in 20 
chain. In configuration where FHM is used - when FHM reset is needed, O-RUs connected through this FHM should be 21 
reset first, then FHM reset can be performed. It is strongly recommended to disable carriers affected by such a reset 22 
procedure prior to the triggering of the reset to minimize the impact on C/U-plane traffic as much as possible. In case an 23 
O-RU connected through FHM requires to be reset - the reset will not impact to other O-RUs. 24 


  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        138 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Note: there is no difference between Hierarchical M -plane architecture and Hybrid M -plane architecture from the 1 
point of reset ordering in either cascade mode (chain topology), or FHM mode (star topology). 2 
Using this approach, a NETCONF client can performs software management on multiple O -RUs. Since this procedure 3 
may require the reset of the O -RU to update the appropriate software file(s) for the O -RUs, the NETCONF client is 4 
recommended to order the software management procedures such that the reset procedure issued against one O-RU shall 5 
not impact the other O-RUs or FHM. 6

14.3 Performance Management 4 
This sub-section provides description of the specific part of Performance Management for shared cell. 5 
14.3.1 Measurement-group 6 
transceiver-stats: 7 
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) has multiple connections to O -DU and O -RU (Cascade/Normal). The baseline O -RU models 8 
permit O-RUs to be defined with multiple ports and multiple transceiver modules. Transceiver module is defined by o -9 
ran-transceiver which refers the p ort-number for these interfaces. Please refer to sub -section 14.5.1 O -RU Information 10 
for Shared Cell. In this case, the O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall be able to report transceiver-stats per port-number. 11 
Rx-window-stats: 12 
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall monitor rx-window-stats per eaxc-id, per transport or per hardware component (O -RU) 13 
because it receives data flow from the north-node. 14 
Note: This version of the specification does support rx-window-stats to monitor the downlink reception window and 15 
doesn’t support monitoring by an O-RU of the uplink traffic from south-node. 16 
Tx-stats: 17 
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall monitor tx-stats per eaxc-id, per transport or per hardware component (O -RU) because it 18 
transmits data flow to the north-node. 19 


  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
Note: This version of the specification does support tx-stats to monitor uplink traffic and doesn’t support monitoring by 1 
an O-RU of the downlink traffic to south-node. 2 
Epe-stats: 3 
O-RU (Cascade / FHM) shall monitor epe-stats per hardware component. 4

14.4 Delay Management 8 
In the shared cell environment, the use of O-RU Adaptive Delay capability is not permitted. The O-DU and each O-RU 9 
have their own delay parameters and supported transmission window and reception window. Also, the topology of the 10 
O-RU configuration can be detected by the topology discovery procedure.  11 
The O-DU can determine the delay budget between itself and the O-RUs considering the O-RUs’ topology and delay 12 
parameters and its own transmission window and reception window. During this discovery, the required processing time 13 
of the O-RU is also considered. The O-RU processing time includes the copy operation for downlink operation, and the 14 
combine operation for uplink operation, and the delay periods for the copy and combine operations are defined as t-15 
copy and t-combine in o-ran-shared-cell.yang module: 16 
t-copy: Corresponding to the maximum FHM or cascade O-RU processing delay between receiving an IQ sample 17 
over the fronthaul interface from the north-node, coping it and transmitting it over the fronthaul interface to the 18 
south-node. 19 
t-combine: Corresponding to the maximum FHM or cascade O-RU processing delay between receiving an IQ sample 20 
over the fronthaul interface from the south-node(s), combing them and transmitting it over the fronthaul interface to 21 
the north-node. 22 
Therefore, based on the above information, the O-DU can determine how many O-RUs are configured to operate in a 23 
shared cell instance. 24 
After the delay budget between the O-DU and the furthest (southern-most) O-RU in the chain is determined, multiple 25 
O-RUs can be configured to operate in between the O-DU and the furthest O-RU. The time budget between the O-DU 26 
and the furthest O-RU is constant and is shared for all O-RUs operating in cascade mode.  27 
For combine function operation, the O-RU shall await the successful reception of the eCPRI frame(s) from the south-28 
node(s). Once the FHM receives the eCPRI frame from all of the south-nodes, the O-RU (FHM) can perform the 29 
combine operation. Once the cascade O-RU receives the eCPRI frame from the south-node, the O-RU can perform the 30 
combine operation using the eCPRI frame and received radio information. The maximum time an O-RU is permitted to 31 
wait for the required eCPRI frames is set by the ta3-prime-max configured by NETCONF client. If the O-RU cannot 32 
commence the combination procedure until a time after the configured ta3-prime-max minus static t-combine, e.g., 33 
due to the delayed reception of eCPRI frame(s), the O-RU shall discard the delayed eCPRI frames if received and 34 
combine other received frames (for FHM mode) or radio information (for Cascade mode). The configurable ta3-prime-35 
max shall be equal to or less than ta3-prime-max-upper-limit which is the capability of O-RU, related to the internal 36 
memory for combine operation. The detail for C/U-plane aspects is described in chapter 11.3 of [2]. 37 
 38 
ta3-prime-max: The latest time that FHM or cascade O-RU is allowed to send UL U-plane message to north-node 39 
relative to reception timing at O-RU antenna. 40 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        145 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
ta3-prime-max-upper-limit: The upper limit for the configurable ta3-prime-max value. This is the capability 1 
information of O-RU that comes from the O-RU internal memory for the combine operation. 2

14.5.1 O-RU Information for Shared Cell 5 
Interfaces to south-node of O-RU with Copy and Combine function 6

interfaces to south-nodes, illustrated below. 8

defined by o-ran-transceiver which refers the port-number for these interfaces. The maximum number of the interfaces 13

layer ietf-interface (type = l2vlan) configured for the ietf-interface (type =ethernetCsmacd) to north-node in section 4.3.  19 
If an interface to a south-node is not used for shared cell scenario, the NETCONF client doesn’t need to configure the 20 
higher layer ietf-interface (type = l2vlan) for it. 21 
Capability of O-RU with Copy and Combine function 22 
The configuration for Copy and Combine function is defined in the o-ran-shared-cell.yang module. The presence of this 23 
yang module signalled in O-RU’s YANG library indicates that O-RU can support the copy and combine function. The 24 
shared-cell-module-cap container includes the information for the internal maximum processing delay for both the 25 
copy function and the combine function required for delay management operations. The shared-cell-module-cap 26 
container also includes the information defining the maximum numbers of copy and combine functions supported. This 27 
information is used by the NETCONF client to determine how many south-nodes can be supported and how many eaxc-28 
ids can be used for copy and combine procedures. It also contains the information defining the compression capability 29 
supported by the FHM. 30

For the cascade mode, the cascade O-RU shall support normal O-RU operations, i.e., radio transmission and reception. 1 
For the FHM mode, the FHM doesn't have the capability for radio transmission and reception. The o-ran-shared-2

14.5.2 Topology Discovery procedure 15 
The O-DU shall determine the topology (adjacency relationships) of O-RUs for the shared cell. In this version of the 16 
specification, only Ethernet based transport of C/U sessions for shared cells is supported. The shared cell topology 17 
discovery procedure operates at the Ethernet layer, using the LBM/LBR connectivity checking procedure defined in 18 
sub-section 4.6 to fill the Ethernet Forwarding Information Base (FIB), and is based on the O-DU recovering the FIB. 19 
The transparent bridge functionality is used in the shared cell capable O-RUs operating in FHM and/or cascade mode. 20 
In a typical operation, an O-DU performs a two-stage procedure for determining the topology: 21 
I. In a first stage, the O-DU performs Ethernet connectivity monitoring on all discovered O-RU MAC addresses, 22 
using the procedures defined in sub-section 4.6.1. The sending of the Ethernet Loopback responses from the 23 
discovered MAC addresses ensures that the transparent bridges in the O-RUs operating in FHM and cascade 24 
mode will automatically learn the MAC addresses switched through these devices.  25 
Note: In addition to Ethernet connectivity monitoring, DHCP discovery, call home and M-plane connection 26 
establishment can also be used to populate information in the FIB and so may be sufficient when an O-RU 27 
only has a single port configured for interfacing to its north-node. 28 
II. In a second stage, the O-DU uses the o-ran-ethernet-forwarding.yang module to discover which MAC 29 
addresses have been learnt by the Ethernet bridge functionality. The O-DU uses the individual Ethernet 30 
forwarding table entries to determine the adjacency relationships. 31 
 32 
The following figure illustrates an example of the MAC address configuration for a set of O-RUs configured in cascade 33 
mode and FHM mode of operations, together with the associated Transparent Bridge FIB tables. 34 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00

14.5.3 Shared Cell Configuration 3 
Shared cell configuration consists of shared cell copy entities and share d cell combine entities. For the shared cell 4 
configuration, the choice-case statement shared-cell-copy-combine-model is used for future enhancement.  5 
Both shared cell copy entities and shared cell combine entities define the transport-flows for the processing elements of 6 
the interface to north-node and the interface to south -node. The combine entities contain the  ta3-prime-max to be used 7 
in delay management as described in sub-section 14.4.  8 
As per conventional o -ran-processing-element.yang, the transport-flow (eth-flow) of the processing element is a 9 
combination of o-du-mac-address, ru-mac-address and vlan-id for legacy eth-flow.  10

14.5.4 U-plane Configuration for FHM mode 9 
For the FHM mode, O-RU (FHM) doesn’t need to have u-plane configuration defined in o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module. 10 
Instead, O-RU (FHM) needs to have s hared-cell specific u-plane configuration. The shared-cell-copy-uplane-config is 11 
the eaxc-id list used by DL C-plane, DL U-plane and UL C-plane traffic. It also contains downlink-radio-frame-offset 12 
and downlink-sfn-offset to define the downlink timing of t =0 for the reception window. The shared-cell-combine-13 
uplane-config is the compression method of the UL U-plane traffic applied to O-RUs within the shared cell network in 14 
shared cell combine function. The compression method is configurable per eaxc-id. It a lso contains downlink-radio-15 
frame-offset, downlink-sfn-offset and n-ta-offset to define the uplink timing of t=0 for the configured ta3-prime-max. 16 
In addition, number-of-prb is also contained for the case that all PRBs in numPrbc are controlled by C-plane message. 17 
FHM may have multiple sets of shared cell networks as described in the Figure 76 E.g., O-RU#2a and O-RU#2b are one 18 
shared cell network. O -RU#2x and O -RU#2y are  another shared cell network. These two shared cell network s are 19 
separated transport layer level definitions using separate processing -element/transport-flows. Nevertheless, the O -RU 20 
Controller shall ensure that the eaxc -id allocation for the shared cell networks shall be unique per link (downlink or 21 
uplink) in one O-RU (FHM). NETCONF client ( O-RU Controller) shall ensure to allocate unique eaxc -id for O-RU(s) 22 
per link within the shared cell network(s) in one O-RU (FHM). 23 
Note: shared-cell-copy-uplane-config and shared-cell-combine-uplane-config are not applicable to the cascade mode. 24 
Instead, o-ran-uplane-conf.yang module is applied. 25 
Note: if the FHM supports the C/U-plane monitoring timer described in section 4.10, then depending on how long the O-26 
DU takes to initiate sending of C/U plane data flows, it may be advisable for the NETCONF client to initially disable the 27 
operation of the timer for the FHM before carrier activation to O-RUs that are south-nodes for the FHM. Such an approach 28 
will avoid the FHM sending spurious alarm notifications triggered by O -DU delays i n initializing the sending of C/U 29 
plane data that exceed the default timer value. Once C/U plane data flows have commenced, the NETCONF client can 30 
re-configure the timer with the desired value and hence activate monitoring of the C/U plane connectivity by the FHM. 31 
14.5.5 Support of Selective Transmission and Reception Function 32 
This section describes M -Plane support for selective transmission and reception function which is specified in chapter 33 
11.2.1 of [2]. There are two things to be introduced for supporting the function from M-Plane perspective; 34 
• Feature which indicates FHM support for selective transmission and reception function 35 
• Configuration parameters which indicate the mapping information between global beamId, O-RU(s) and O-RU 36 
local beamId. 37 
If FHM indicates the feature “SELECTIVE-BEAM-ID” to O-DU, O-DU can configure the mapping information between 38 
global beamId, O-RU(s) and O-RU local beamId to the FHM to use selective transmission and reception function. For 39 
configuring the information, mapping-table-for-selective-beam-id is used. 40

limited to 2. The first cascade FHM nearest to O-DU is named FHM#1, the second FHM is named FHM#2. 45

Chapter 15 Configured Subscriptions 5 
15.1 Introduction 6 
The support by an O -RU of configured subscriptions is an optional capability, advertised by the O -RU indicating it 7 
supports the ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model [37] in its YANG library together with the configured feature. 8 
This capability enables an O -RU Controller to i nstall a subscription via configuration of the O -RU’s datastore. 9 
Importantly, the lifetime of such a configured subscription is not limited to the lifetime of the NETCONF session used to 10 
establish it, enabling a configured subscription to persist even when  an O-RU has been temporarily disconnected from 11 
the network.  12 
The ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model defines a transport agnostic mechanism for subscribing to and receiving 13 
content from an event stream in an O-RU. An O-RU that supports configured subscriptions shall also support the encode-14 
json feature together with the augmentation of the ietf-subscribed-notifications YANG model by the o-ran-ves-15 
subscribed-notifications YANG model.  16 
15.2 Description 17 
An O-RU controller discovers the event-streams supported by an O-RU. The O-RU Controller then establishes a 18 
configured subscription to a particular event-stream.  19 
Note, the same NACM privileges defined in Sub-section 3.4 shall also be used by the O-RU in determining 20 
whether an O-RU controller has privileges to establish a configured subscription to a particular event-stream. 21 
Based on configured subscriptions, the O-RU sends asynchronous notifications over HTTPS to the configured Event-22 
Collector. This capability can be used with any existing YANG notification, e.g., defined in YANG models published 23 
by the O-RAN Alliance or imported from other organizations.   24 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        154 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
15.3 Procedure 1 
 2 
Figure 78:Message sequence exchange for provisioning a configured notification 3 
Pre-condition: A NETCONF sessions is established between the O-RU and an O-RU Controller. 4 
 5 
1. The O-RU controller gets the streams container and discovers the event-streams supported by an O-RU 6 
2. The O-RU controller uses the “edit-config” RPC to configure a subscription to an event-stream. The 7 
RPC includes the receiver container augmented with the notification-recipient schema node that 8 
encodes the URI of the Event-Collector. 9 
3. If the O-RU controller has the correct privileges, the O-RU accepts the configured subscription 10 
4. As the lifetime of the configured subscription is not limited by the lifetime of the NETCONF session, 11 
the O-RU controller may terminate the NETCONF session without causing the subscription to be 12 
suspended. 13 
5. After a subscription is successfully established, the O-RU immediately sends a "subscription-started" 14 
notification to the Event-Collector, according to RFC8639 [37] clause 2.5. 15 
6. Upon an event that triggers a YANG notification, the O-RU sends a notification over HTTPS , 16 
according to RFC8639 clause 2.5. 17 
Post-condition: The Event-Collector is able to update its operational-state datastore with the information received in the 18 
notification. 19 
15.4 Notification Encoding  20 
The O-RU shall support JSON encoding as specified in RFC 7951 [38]. An example notification object generated using 21 
the o-ran-file-management.yang model and encoded following RFC 7951 is illustrated in Figure 79. 22

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        155 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
 1 
Figure 79:Example of a JSON encoded YANG Notification 2 
15.5 Notification Transport 3 
As described in RFC8639 clause 2.5.7, an O-RU supporting configured subscriptions must provide a YANG data model 4 
capturing the necessary transport-specific configuration parameters. O-RAN compliant Event-Producers shall support 5 
the o-ran-ves-subscribed-notifications YANG model.  6 
For transport, the notification JSON objects encoded according to sub-section 15.4 are further encapsulated in VES 7 
events. In order to enable the notifications sent to the Event-Collector to retain their native notification format/schema 8 
as defined in O-RAN, IETF and other YANG models, the ONAP/VES header is used to enable the decoupling of the 9 
notification payload from the overall VES event format, as illustrated in the figure above.  10 
The VES common header shall include the following fields: 11 
- The value of the eventName field shall be set to “ORU-YANG/<model-identifier>:<notification-identifier>” 12 
- The value of the eventID field shall be set to “stndDefined-ORU-YANG-nnnnnnnnn", where nnnnnnnnnn 13 
represents the integer key for the event 14 
- The value of the sourceName and reportingEntityName fields shall both be set to the value of the ru-instance-15 
id leaf defined in the o-ran-operations YANG model.  16 
{ "ietf-restconf:notification": { 
    "eventTime": "2020-11-11T20:20:00Z",

15.6 Monitoring the Communications Channel between O-RU and 7 
Event-Collector 8 
An O-RU controller can use the NETCONF monitoring capability described in sub-section 3.6 to trigger the repeated 9 
sending of a supervision-notification by the O-RU to a subscribed O-RU Controller to ensure the channel is 10 
operational and able to transport asynchronous notifications using NETCONF. An equivalent capability is required to 11 
be supported by those O-RUs that support configured subscriptions transported using JSON/HTTPS, to enable the 12 
monitoring of the communications channel from the O-RU to the Event-Collector. The format of the heartbeat 13 
notifications is identical to the Event-Collector Notification Format determined for the operation of pnfRegistration as 14

15.6.1 Heartbeat Encoding 3 
The VES common header shall include the following fields: 4 
- The value of the sourceName and reportingEntityName fields shall both be set to the value of the ru-instance-5 
id leaf defined in the o-ran-operations YANG model.  6 
An example heartbeat encoding is illustrated in Figure 82. 7 
 8 
Figure 82:Example of a JSON encoded VES Event Carrying a Heartbeat Notification 9 
15.6.2 Heartbeat Control 10 
Control of the heartbeat does not use the configured subscriptions capability. An O-RU controller configures heartbeat 11 
operation using the o-ran-supervision YANG model. An O-RU Controller shall configure the heartbeat-recipient-id to 12 
the address(es) of the Heartbeat Event-Collector and optionally configure the heartbeat-interval leaf to a non-default 13 
heartbeat interval. In order to terminate operation of the monitoring the communications channel between O-RU and the 14 
Event-Collector, the O-RU Controller shall delete the configuration in the event-collector-monitoring container. 15

In contrast to the monitoring of NETCONF connectivity described in sub -section 3.6 which define O -RU procedures 4 
when monitoring of NETCONF connectivity fails, there is no equivalent O -RU functionality defined if an O -RU 5 
determines that monitoring of the communications channel between O-RU and event-collector fails, e.g., if the O-RU is 6 
unable to establish a TLS connection to the event-collector.  7 
Operation of the SMO when it determines that the monitoring of the communications channel between an O -RU and 8 
event-collector fails is out of scope of this specification. 9

Annex A Alarm definition 1 
This section contains example alarms which may be reported. 2 
Obviously, alarms that are not applicable in given HW design or SW configuration shall not be reported. For example, 3 
alarms related to fan monitoring are applicable to HW variants with fans. 4 
In many cases alarm detection method is HW specific. It is assumed that alarm detection method is reliable to avoid 5 
undetected alarms and false alarms. It is also expected that the NETCONF Server is applying mechanisms to avoid 6 
unreasonably fast toggling of alarms’ state. 7 
 8 
The example alarms table has following columns: 9 
Fault id – Numerical identifier of alarm. This ID shall be used in <alarm-notif> message (fault-id parameter). 10 
Name – Name of the alarm. 11 
Meaning – Description of alarm, describes high level meaning of the alarm. 12 
Start condition – Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to generate alarm. If filtering time is needed, then it must be 13 
defined in this column. 14 
Cancel condition – Defines conditions which must be fulfilled to cancel alarm. If filtering time is needed, then it must be 15 
defined in this column. 16 
NETCONF Server actions on detection – Defines actions of the NETCONF Server after alarm has been detected. 17 
NETCONF Server actions on cancel – Defines actions of NETCONF Server after alarm has been cancelled. 18 
System recovery actions – Describes gNB level recovery actions of the NETCONF Client after alarm has been indicated 19 
by NETCONF Server. This field is informative only; actions taken by the NETCONF Client are not restricted nor defined 20 
in this document. System recovery action “Reset” refers to NETCONF Client forcing reset of O-RU. 21 
Source – Defines possible sources of the alarm (alarm is within O-RU). The following are XML enco ding provides 22 
examples of the component names defined in various YANG modules that may be alarm sources inside the O-RU. 23 
- < hardware xmlns= "urn:o-ran:hardware:1.0"><component><o-ran-name/></component></hardware> 24 
- <fan-tray xmlns= "urn:o-ran:fan:1.0"><fan-state><name/></fan-state></fan-tray> 25 
- <sync xmlns= "urn:o-ran:sync:1.0"><gnss-state><name/></gnss-state></sync> 26 
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><input><name/></input></external-io> 27 
- <external-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:externalio:1.0”><output><name/></output></external-io> 28 
- <ald-ports-io xmlns= "urn:o-ran:ald-port:1.0”><ald-port><name/></ald-port></ald-ports-io> 29 
- <port-transceivers xmlns= "urn:o-ran:transceiver:1.0”><port-transceiver-data><name/></ port-30 
transceiver-data ></port-transceivers> 31 
- <interfaces xmlns= "urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:yang:ietf-32 
interfaces”><interface><name/></interface></interfaces> 33 
- <processing-elements xmlns= "urn:o-ran:processing-element.1.0”><ru-elements><name/></ru-34 
elements></processing-elements> 35 
- <-ran-uplane-conf xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-tx-links><name/></low-level-tx-links></ 36 
o-ran-uplane-conf> 37 
- <o-ran-uplane-conf xmlns= "urn:o-ran:uplane-conf.1.0”><low-level-rx-links><name/></low-level-rx-38 
links></o-ran-uplane-conf> 39 
 40 
Note: If Source will not fit to any of above, or is empty, it means that external device (like Antenna Line Devices) cause 41 
an alarm (fault is out of the O-RU). Then additional text in alarm notification is needed to clearly say what may be possible 42 
fault source. 43 
 44 
Severity – Defines severity of the alarm [30]. 45 
Critical – sub unit for which alarm has been generated is not working and cannot be used. 46

O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00

Minor – sub unit for which alarm has been generated is still working. 2

B.1 Transceiver Statistics  8 
The transceiver-measurement includes the performance measurement of transceivers as shown in the following table. 9 
 10 
measurement-object Description 
RX_POWER Measured Rx input power in mW for SFP or lane 1 of QSFP

RX_POWER_LANE_4 Measured Rx input power in mW for lane 4 of QSFP 
TX_POWER Measured Tx input power in mW for SFP or lane 1 of QSFP.  
TX_POWER_LANE_2 Measured Tx input power in mW for lane 2 of QSFP 
TX_POWER_LANE_3 Measured Tx input power in mW for lane 3 of QSFP

TX_BIAS_COUNT_LANE_4 Internally measured Tx Bias Current in mA for lane 4 of QSFP 
VOLTAGE Internally measured transceiver supply voltage in mV 
TEMPARATURE Internally measured optional laser temperature in degrees Celsius. 
Table 9: Transceiver Measurements 11 
 12 
B.1.1 Statistics Calculation 13 
When configured by the NETCONF client, the O-RU captures value of monitored parameters. Then the O-RU calculates 14 
x = f(s), where f(s) is a function selected for specific statistics instance. The function f(s) can be one of the following:  15 
• f(s) = s  16 
• f(s) = LOG10(s),  17 
where LOG10(s) is logarithm with base 10. To avoid issues with infinity, the O-RU assumes that for s < 10 -128 value of 18 
LOG10(s) is -128. 19 
 20 
The value of x = f(s) is applied to first, latest, min and max values; related timestamps are also updated; frequency table 21 
is updated as described in the following section. 22 
 23 

  
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN Alliance e.V.  
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ        168 
O-RAN.WG4.MP.0-v07.00 
When local measurement interval, which is not same as transceiver-measurement-interval of the measurement-object, 1 
passes the O-RU captures value of a monitored parameter (s). Then the O-RU calculates x = f(s), where f is a function 2 
selected for specific parameter.  The local measurement interval is up to the O-RU implementation matter and typically 3 
around 10 sec – 60 sec at earliest. 4 
  5 
The value of x = f(s) is applied to latest value; related timestamp is updated.   6 
The O-RU updates statistics:  7 
• If x < min value then x is applied to min value and related timestamp is updated.  8 
• If x > max value then x is applied to max value and related timestamp is updated.  9 
• Value of x is used to update frequency table as described in section Frequency Table below.  10 
 11 
After updates O-RU waits another interval to elapse. 12 
B.1.2 Frequency Table Generation  13 
Let n = bin-count, a = lower-bound, b = upper-bound, x = f(s) where s is value of monitored parameter and f is a 14 
function selected for statistics via parameter function.   15 
 16 
• If n = 0 then frequency table is empty and is not updated.   17 
• If n > 0 there are n bins: hk where k = 0...n-1. Initial value of each bin is zero (hk = 0 for k = 0...n-1).  18 
• If x < a then bin h0 is incremented.   19 
• If b ≤ x and n > 1 then bin hn-1 is incremented.  20 
• If a ≤ x and x < b and n > 2 then bin hk is incremented for k such that   21 
• k-1 ≤ (n-2) * (x-a) / (b-a) < k.  22 
 23 
Note value of bin should saturate at maximum without overflowing (the value is not incremented above 232-1).  24 
Equivalently:  25 
 26 
• For k = 0, hk is a number of values x such that x < a. 27 
• For k = 1 ... n-2, hk is a number of values x such that  28 
• a + (b-a) * (k-1) / (n-2) ≤ x < a + (b-a) * (k) / (n-2).   29 
• For k = n-1, hk is a number of values x such that b ≤ x.   30 
 31 
Example:   32 
 33 
function = LOG10, bin-count = 14, lower-bound = -12, upper-bound = 0 34 
 35 
• parameter value s = 0, x = f(0) = -128, -128 < -12 = a 
  h0 is incremented   36 
• parameter value s = 1e-12, x = f(1e-12) = -12, (14-2)*(-12-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*0/12 < 1  
  h1 is incremented   37 
• parameter value s = 9.99e -12, x = f(9.99e -12) = -11.0004, (14-2)*(-11.0004-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*0.9996/12 < 1 38 
 h1 is incremented  39 
• parameter value s = 1e-1, x = f(1e-1) = -1, (14-2)*(-1-(-12))/(0-(-12)) = 12*11/12 < 12 
  h12 is incremented  40 
• parameter value s = 1, x = f(1) = 0, 0 ≥ 0 = b  
  h13 is incremented  41 
 42

B.5 Symbol RSSI Statistics  1 
B.5.1 Statistics Calculation 2 
The symbol -rssi-stats is the time domain RSSI per symbol, the reference point for the TD -RSSI shall be the antenna 3 
connector of the O-RU. The value of Received Signal Strength Indicator(RSSI) per rx-array-carrier per configured OFDM 4 
symbol is measured. T he RSSI shall be calculated as the linear average of the total received power observed in the 5 
configured OFDM symbol in the measurement bandwidth from all sources including co-channel serving and non-serving 6 
cells, adjacent channel interference, thermal noise, etc, over the total number of antenna elements of the array. The unit 7 
of the reported RSSI is dBm. 8 
If analog or hybrid beamforming is enabled, the beamId used for RSSI measurement is: 9 
        - When there is allocation of a beamId in this symbol, O-RU use that beamId for RSSI measurement;  10 
        -  When there is no allocation of a beamId in this symbol, it  is up to O -RU implementation, for example,  the O-RU 11 
can choose to use a common beamId or use a previous allocated beamId"; 12 
measurement-object Description 
ALL-UL-SYMBOLS Measure and report symbol-rssi separately for all UL symbols in 
every configured number of slots (as defined by 'period' in 
'symbol-rssi-measurement-objects'. And the UL symbols are 
decided by 'configurable-tdd-pattern', 'static-srs-configuration', 
'static-prach-configuration', and 'dataDirection' in the C-plane 
messages. 
This option is recommended for static TDD case. If this option is 
used in dynamic TDD case, then O-RU measures only the 
allocates UL symbols because O-RU may not know 'candidate UL 
symbols' which are not allocated. 
CONFIGURED-
SYMBOLS 
Measure and report symbol-rssi separately for all configured 
symbols as defined by the leaf-list 'symbol-index'. 
This can be used for non-dynamic TDD as well as dynamic TDD 
cases, the O-RU should measure all configured symbols, 
irrespective of whether the UL symbol is allocated or not. 
If a c-plane message indicates a symbol within the 'symbol-index' 
list to be a DL symbol,  O-RU shall not measure rssi on this 
symbol. 
Table 13: Symbol RSSI Measurements 13

Annex D YANG Module Graphical Representation 2 
The different released version of the set of YANG modules for the O-RU can be downloaded from O-RAN’s website 3 
http://www.o-ran.org/specifications/ . The YANG models are available in a zip file, whose name is used to represent the 4 
version of the YANG model and follows the numerical format defined in subsection 1.1 with the periods replaced with 5 
“-”, i.e., YANG models for release 1.0.0 of the M -Plane specification are available in the file 1 -0-0.zip. This zip file 6 
includes all published revisions of the YANG models supporting a particular release of the M-Plane specification. 7 
This Annex provides a set of “tree -views” of the modules to provide a simplified graphical representation of the data 8 
models. These trees have been automatically generated using the pyang  YANG validator tool. If there are any 9 
inconsistencies between the tree representation in this Annex and the yang models, the yang models shall take precedence. 10

Section 4: TERM AND TERMINATION 24 
4.1 This Agreement shall remain in force, unless early terminated according to this Section 4. 25 
4.2 O-RAN Alliance on behalf of its Members, Contributors and Academic Contributors may terminate this Agreement 26 
if Adopter materially breaches this Agreement and does not cure or is not capable of curing such breach within thirty 27 
(30) days after being given notice specifying the breach. 28 
4.3 Sections 1, 3, 5 - 11 of this Agreement shall survive any termination of this Agreement. Under surviving Section 3, 29 
after termination of this Agreement, Adopter will continue to grant licenses (a) to entities who become Adopters after 30 
the date of termination; and (b) for future versions of ORAN Specifications that are backwards compatible with the 31 
version that was current as of the date of termination. 32

care. Any disclosure by Adopter to its Affiliates, contractors and consultants should be subject to an obligation of 36 
confidentiality at least as restrictive as those contained in this Section. The foregoing obligation shall not apply to any 37 
information which is: (1) rightfully known by Adopter without any limitation on use or disclosure prior to disclosure; 38 
(2) publicly available through no fault of Adopter; (3) rightfully received without a duty of confidentiality; (4) disclosed 39 
by O-RAN Alliance or a Member, Contributor or Academic Contributor to a third party without a duty of 40 
confidentiality on such third party; (5) independently developed by Adopter; (6) disclosed pursuant to the order of a 41 
court or other authorized governmental body, or as required by law, provided that Adopter provides reasonable prior 42 
written notice to O-RAN Alliance, and cooperates with O-RAN Alliance and/or the applicable Member, Contributor or 43 
Academic Contributor to have the opportunity to oppose any such order; or (7) disclosed by Adopter with O-RAN 44 
Alliance’s prior written approval. 45
